Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Sale is Concluded by Offer and Acceptance in the Past Tense
Stating the rule and proving it with Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a sale is valid only with past-tense offer and acceptance and identify the Quranic and Prophetic proofs for this requirement.

Core Idea
A sale is only binding when offer and acceptance are in the past tense — no mere promises.

This lesson addresses one of the foundational conditions for a valid sale in Hanafi fiqh: that the offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) must be expressed in the past tense. The text from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains why this is required and supports it with Quranic and Prophetic proofs. Understanding this condition is essential for distinguishing a legally binding contract from a mere promise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on the validity of a sale contract. Identify that the act is 'bay' (sale) and the ruling is that it is concluded (valid) when ijab and qabul are in the past tense.
The specific condition is added: both expressions must be in the past tense.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (2:275) as general proof that sale is permitted, and two hadith from Tirmidhi that demonstrate the practice of using past tense in sale transactions.
The Quran gives general permissibility; the hadith show the required form.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the Quran, the permissibility of sale is established. From the hadith, the specific use of past tense (ishtara, akhadhtu) indicates that the Prophet and Companions used past tense to make the contract binding immediately.
The hadith are used as evidence for the condition, not just permissibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow present tense or other expressions of consent. The text does not detail their proof but notes the difference.
The Hanafi position is strict: past tense is required for immediate effect.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this as the mufta bihi position, emphasising that present tense only creates a promise, not a binding contract.
The wisdom is to prevent uncertainty and give the contract immediate effect.

(1) فعل ماضی کے استعمال کرنے سے بات پکی ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ عربی زبان میں یا فعل ماضی ہے یا فعل مضارع ہے اور فعل مضارع کا ترجمہ حال ہے یا استقبال، پس اگر استقبال کے معنی لے لے تو بیچنے یا خریدنے کا صرف وعدہ ہوگا ، با ضابطہ بیچنا اور خرید نا نہیں ہوگا اس لئے بات پکی کرنے کے لئے فعل ماضی ہی کا صیغہ استعمال کرنا ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے قال لى العداء بن خالد بن هوذه الا اقرنك كتابا كتبه لي رسول الله قال قلت بلى فاخرج لي كتابا هذا ما اشترى العداء بن خالد بن هوذه من محمد رسول الله اشترى منه عبدا او امة لاداء ولا غائلة ولا خبثة (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی کتابة الشروط ص ۲۳۰ نمبر ۱۲۱۶) اس حدیث میں اشتری فعل ماضی کا صیغہ استعمال کیا گیا ہے تا کہ بات پکی ہو۔ پھر خرید و فروخت کو لکھ لیا گیا تا کہ اور یکے ہو جائیں (۳) اور ایک حدیث میں فعل ماضی کا صیغہ استعمال کیا گیا ہے عن انس بن مالك ان رسول الله باع حلسا و قدحا وقال من يشترى هذا الحلس والقدح؟ فقال رجل اخذتهما بدرهم (ج) (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی بیع من یزید ص ۲۳۰ نمبر ۱۳۱۸) اس حدیث میں خریدنے والے نے اخذ تہما بدرھم کہا ہے اور فعل ماضی کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہے۔ اس لئے بیچ میں فعل ماضی استعمال کرنا ضروری ہے اصل معاملات میں بات کی ہونا ضروری ہے (۲) بیع اور شرار فعل ماضی کے صیغے سے ادا کرے، اور ایجاب اور قبول ہو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے  حاشیہ : (الف) اللہ تعالی نے بیع کو حلال کیا اور سود کو حرام کیا ہے (ب) مجھے عداء بن خالد بن ھوذہ نے فرمایا کیا میں آپ کے سامنے ایسا خط نہ پڑھوں جس کو میرے لئے لکھوایا ہے۔ میں نے کہا ہاں ! تو ایک خط نکالا (جس میں یہ لکھا تھا یہ وہ ہے کہ عداء بن خالد بن ھوڈو نے محمد سے غلام یا باندی خریدی جس میں بیماری نہیں، دھوکہ نہیں اور خباثت نہیں ( ج ) حضور نے جھول اور پیالہ بیچا، فرمایا اس جھول اور پیالے کو کون خریدے گا ؟ ایک نے کہا ان دونوں کو ایک درہم کے بدلے میں نے خریدا۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Part Two. Book of Sales. [20](1) The sale is concluded by offer and acceptance when both are in the past tense. ... Necessary note: Bay' is derived from ba'a - he sold, meaning exchanging property for property. ... The proof that sale is permissible is the verse: Allah has permitted sale and forbidden usury (2:275). ... This verse shows that sale is permissible. The book of sales is among transactions. Therefore many issues in it are based on the common practice of people. ... (1) The sale is concluded by offer and acceptance when both are in the past tense. ... That is, one person says 'I bought' and the other says 'I sold', then the sale is concluded, but condition is that both expressions are in the past tense. (1) Using past tense makes the matter firm. Because in Arabic, verb is either past or present, and present tense indicates present or future, so if future meaning is taken, it would be only a promise to sell or buy, not an actual sale. Therefore to make the matter firm, past tense must be used. (2) There is a hadith: 'Adda' ibn Khalid ibn Hawdha said to me: Shall I not recite to you a letter that the Messenger of Allah wrote for me? I said: Yes. So he brought out a letter: This is what 'Adda' ibn Khalid ibn Hawdha bought from Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah. He bought from him a slave or slave-girl, there is no disease, no fraud, no evil. (Tirmidhi, chapter on writing conditions, page 230, no. 1216). In this hadith, 'ishtara' (he bought) is past tense to make it firm. Then the sale was written down for more certainty. (3) Another hadith uses past tense: On the authority of Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah sold a blanket and a cup and said: Who will buy this blanket and cup? A man said: I have taken them for one dirham. (Tirmidhi, chapter on sale by auction, page 230, no. 1318). In this hadith, the buyer said 'akhadhtuhuma' (I have taken them), which is past tense. Therefore using past tense in sale is necessary to make the transaction binding. ... (2) The sale and purchase should be performed with past tense, and offer and acceptance done. The reason for this is... Footnote: (a) Allah has permitted sale and forbidden usury. (b) ... (c) ...
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri begins the Book of Sales (Kitab al-Buyu) by stating the fundamental ruling: a sale is concluded by offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) when both are expressed in the past tense (lafz al-madi). The author explains that bay' etymologically means exchange of property for property. The permissibility of sale is proven by the Quranic verse 2:275. The author notes that since sales are transactions based on common practice, not every issue requires a specific hadith; many rulings are derived from general principles. However, to establish the principle itself, proof is sought. The ruling requires the past tense because Arabic verbs either indicate a completed action (past) or an incomplete one (present/future). Using the present tense would only indicate a promise, not a concluded contract. Two hadith from Tirmidhi are cited: one where the Prophet (SAW) had a letter documenting a sale using 'ishtara' (he bought), and another where a buyer said 'akhadhtuhuma' (I have taken them) – both past tense. Thus, for a sale to be binding, the parties must use the past tense in their offer and acceptance. The Hanafi school emphasizes this strict requirement for immediate contractual effect.

Key Terms
بيع (bay'): The exchange of property for property (مال کے بدلے میں مال دینا)
إيجاب (ijab): The offer made by one party initiating the contract
قبول (qabul): The acceptance by the other party
فعل ماضي (fi'l madi): The past tense verb form indicating a completed action

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what verb form is required for both offer and acceptance in a sale contract?
A) Present tense
B) Future tense
C) Past tense
D) Imperative mood

Key Takeaway
A sale is only concluded when offer and acceptance are in the past tense, ensuring an immediate binding contract rather than a promise.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Sale Concluded by Offer and Acceptance in Past Tense
Ruling with proof on the condition of past tense in contract formation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of past tense for offer and acceptance in a Hanafi sale contract and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A sale is only binding when both offer and acceptance use the past tense—present tense is merely a promise.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling in Hanafi sales law: the requirement of past tense for offer and acceptance. Understanding this condition is crucial because it distinguishes a concluded contract from a mere promise. We will explore the textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that the Hanafi school relies upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The matn states that the sale is concluded (yan'aqid) by ijab and qabul if both are in the past tense (madi). This is a condition for the contract's formation (in'iqad).
The term 'yan'aqid' indicates the contract becomes binding upon fulfillment of this condition.
2
Locate the primary proof from Quran
The verse 'And Allah made sale lawful and prohibited usury' (2:275) establishes the general permissibility of sale. It does not specify the tense, but it sets the foundation for the ruling.
This verse is cited to show that sale is not inherently prohibited, but its specifics come from Sunnah.
3
Examine the hadith proofs from the Sunnah
Three hadiths are cited: the written contract of 'Adda' ibn Khalid using 'ishtara' (past), the sale of the rug and cup where the buyer said 'akhadhtuhuma' (past), and the Prophet's request 'ba'nih' (sell it to me) to Ibn Umar, which in context indicates a past transaction.
These demonstrate the actual practice of the Prophet and companions using past tense.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse proves the legality of sale. The hadiths indicate the proper form: in each transaction, the parties used past tense verbs, showing that this is the required mode for a binding contract.
The imperative 'ba'nih' is interpreted as initiating a past transaction, not a future promise.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools, like the Shafi'i, accept present tense if intention is clear. The Hanafi school strictly requires past tense to ensure a definitive commitment and avoid ambiguity.
This difference affects the validity of contracts in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيع ينعقد بالايجاب والقبول اذا كانا بلفظ الماضي. وأحل الله البيع وحرم الربا. قال لي العداء بن خالد بن هوذه: ألا أقرنك كتابا كتبه لي رسول الله؟ قال: قلت بلى، فأخرج لي كتابا هذا ما اشترى العداء بن خالد بن هوذه من محمد رسول الله اشترى منه عبدا أو أمة لا داء ولا غائلة ولا خبثة. عن أنس بن مالك أن رسول الله باع حلسا وقدحا وقال: من يشتري هذا الحلس والقدح؟ فقال رجل: أخذتهما بدرهم. عن ابن عمر قال: كنا مع النبي في سفر فكنت على بكر صعب لعمر... فقال النبي لعمر: بعنيه، قال: هو لك يا رسول الله.
Sale is concluded by offer and acceptance if both are in the past tense. And Allah made sale lawful and prohibited usury. 'Adda' ibn Khalid ibn Huwaydha said to me: Shall I read to you a letter that the Messenger of Allah wrote for me? He said: I said yes, so he brought out a letter: This is what 'Adda' ibn Khalid ibn Huwaydha bought from Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah; he bought from him a slave or a slave-girl, with no disease, no treachery, and no bad character. From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah sold a rug and a cup and said: Who will buy this rug and cup? A man said: I take them for a dirham. From Ibn 'Umar: We were with the Prophet on a journey, and I was on a difficult young camel of 'Umar... The Prophet said to 'Umar: Sell it to me. He said: It is for you, O Messenger of Allah.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the condition of past tense in offer and acceptance for a valid sale. The matn states that a sale is concluded (yan'aqid) by offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), provided both are in the past tense (madi). The commentary then provides proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The Quranic verse (2:275) establishes the permissibility of sale, and the hadiths demonstrate the practice of the Prophet ﷺ using past tense verbs in sale transactions. The hadith from 'Adda' ibn Khalid shows a written contract using 'ishtara' (bought), indicating the past tense. The hadith from Anas shows the buyer using 'akhadhtuhuma' (I took them) in the past tense. The hadith from Ibn Umar shows the Prophet using 'ba'nih' (sell it to me) in the command form, which is interpreted as indicating a past transaction in context. The key point is that the past tense is necessary for binding commitment, as the present tense implies a promise for the future, not a concluded contract.

Key Terms
ایجاب (ijab): The first statement made by one party in a contract, expressing willingness to sell or buy.
قبول (qabul): The second statement by the other party indicating acceptance of the offer.
فعل ماضی (fi'l madi): Past tense verb, indicating a completed action; used in contract to show immediate binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required tense for offer and acceptance in a Hanafi sale contract?
A) Present tense
B) Future tense
C) Past tense
D) Any tense with clear intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, offer and acceptance must be expressed in the past tense to form a binding contract; present tense indicates a promise only.

Khiyar al-Majlis: The Option of the Session
Rulings on khiyar al-majlis and lapsing of offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-majlis and explain the consequence of leaving the session before acceptance.

Core Idea
Acceptance must happen in the same session; leaving voids the offer. The session ends when parties separate.

In Hanafi sales law, after an offer is made, the offeree has the right to deliberate during the session. However, this right expires when either party leaves. The following passage from the classical text establishes this rule and supports it with a hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on khiyar al-majlis
Read the passage and note the specific legal effect: the offeree has the option to accept or reject, but only while both parties remain in the session. Leaving before acceptance renders the offer void.
2
Locate the dalil from the hadith
The passage cites the hadith of Ibn Umar. Identify how this hadith is used as evidence for the ruling.
3
Analyze how the hadith supports the ruling
The Prophet ﷺ made an offer and Ibn Umar accepted immediately in the same session. The absence of any mention of leaving indicates that acceptance must occur in the session; otherwise the offer would lapse.
This is wajh al-dalalah: the implicit indication that the session is the timeframe for acceptance.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the offeror can revoke at any time and the session doesn't extend beyond immediate exchange. Recognize this difference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (acceptance in same session, leaving voids offer) is the relied-upon view in the school.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا اوجب احد المتعاقدين البيع فالآخر بالخيار ان شاء قبل في المجلس وان شاء رده. فايهما قام من المجلس قبل القبول بطل الايجاب. عن ابن عمر قال: كنا مع النبي في سفر فكنت على بكر صعب لعمر... فقال النبي لعمر: بعنيه، قال: هو لك يا رسول الله.
When one of the two contracting parties makes an offer of sale, the other has the option: if he wishes, he may accept in the session, and if he wishes, he may reject it. Whichever of them leaves the session before acceptance, the offer becomes void. From Ibn 'Umar: We were with the Prophet on a journey, and I was on a difficult young camel of 'Umar... The Prophet said to 'Umar: Sell it to me. He said: It is for you, O Messenger of Allah.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents two interrelated rulings on the offer-acceptance process. First, after an offer (ijab) is made, the other party has the 'option of the session' (khiyar al-majlis): he may accept or reject, but only while both parties remain in the same physical session (majlis). Second, if either party leaves the session before acceptance, the offer becomes void (batil). The commentary cites the hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet ﷺ made an offer to 'Umar and he accepted immediately in the session, illustrating the principle. The reasoning is that the session provides a reasonable time for consideration; extending it indefinitely would cause hardship, while requiring immediate acceptance would be too restrictive. The session is defined by the customary gathering (majlis al-'aqd), which may vary in duration. If the offeror is absent via letter or messenger, the session is considered from the time the message is received.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): Option or choice; here it refers to the offeree's right to accept or reject the offer during the session.
مجلس (majlis): The physical session or meeting where the contract is negotiated; it ends when the parties separate.
بطل (batala): Becomes void; the offer is no longer valid and cannot be accepted after leaves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the offeree leaves the session without accepting the offer?
A) The offer remains valid until the next day
B) The offer becomes void and cannot be accepted later
C) The offeror must renew the offer in writing
D) The offeree can still accept via messenger

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, acceptance must occur in the same session; leaving before acceptance voids the offer entirely.

Khiyar al-Qabul: Session-Based Acceptance in Sales
Ruling on the counterparty's option to accept or reject in the session after an offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-qabul and apply it to scenarios involving session-based acceptance.

Core Idea
After an offer, the offeree must accept or reject within the same session; when the session ends, the offer lapses.

In Hanafi sale contracts, mutual consent is expressed through offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). The timing of acceptance is critical: it must occur in the same gathering (majlis) as the offer. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, the wisdom behind the session requirement, and an exception for sales by mutual delivery (bai' ta'ati).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the acceptance (qabul) after an offer (ijab). The ruling: the offeree has the option (khiyar) to accept or reject, but acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer.
This is called khiyar al-qabul.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari 2115) where the Prophet said 'Sell it to me' and Umar replied 'It is for you' in the same gathering.
The hadith demonstrates the requirement of session-based acceptance.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'bi'ni' (sell to me) is an offer, and 'huwa laka' (it is for you) is acceptance, both uttered in the same session, proving that acceptance must be in the session.
4
Note the exception: bai' ta'ati
If goods are exchanged without verbal ijab and qabul but with mutual consent (e.g., handing over item and price), the sale is valid because actions indicate consent.
This is a valid sale even without spoken words.
5
Evaluate the wisdom
The session requirement balances the offeree's need to think and the offeror's need not to wait indefinitely; it prevents both parties' hardship.
The session is the shari'ah criterion for acceptance.

فاذا اوجب احد المتعاقدين البيع فالآخر بالخيار ان شاء قبل في المجلس وان شاء رده [۸۲۲] کہ بائع اور مشتری کی رضامندی کے بغیر بیج نہیں ہوگی اور اس رضامندی کا اظہار ایجاب اور قبول سے ہوگا۔ اس لئے ایجاب اور قبول کی ضرورت ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت موجود ہے عن ابن عمر قال كنا مع النبي الله في سفر فكنت على بكر صعب لعمر ... فقال النبي لعمر بعنيه قال هو لک یا رسول الله الا الله) الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اشتری شد یا فوهب من ساعته قبل ان حفر قاص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۱۱۵) اس حدیث میں حضور نے بعنیہ کہ کر ایجاب کیا اور حضرت عمر نے ھو لک یا رسول اللہ کہہ کر قبول کیا۔ اس لئے بیچ میں ایجاب اور قبول ضروری ہیں۔ نوٹ اگر بائع مبیع دیدے اور مشتری لے لے اور قیمت معلوم ہو اور کچھ ایجاب وقبول نہ کرے تو یہ بیچ تعاطی ہے۔ اس سے بھی بیع ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ رضامندی ہوگئی اور دلالتہ ایجاب اور قبول ہو گئے۔ [۸](۲) پس جبکہ خرید و فروخت کرنے والوں میں سے ایک نے بیع کا ایجاب کیا تو دوسرے کو اختیار ہے چاہے مجلس میں قبول کرے اور اگر چاہے تو اس کو رد کر دے۔ تشریح ایک کے بیع کے ایجاب کرنے کے بعد دوسرے کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کو قبول کرے چاہے اس کو رد کر دے لیکن قبول کرنے کا اختیار مجلس باقی رہنے تک ہی ہو گا۔ اگر مجلس ختم ہوگئی تو اب قبول کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ مجلس چاہے کتنی لمبی ہو اس کو جمع للمفرقات قرار دیا ہے۔ کیونکہ فورا قبول کرنے کی شرط لگا دے تو قبول کرنے والے کو سوچنے کا موقع نہیں ہوگا، اور مجلس کے بعد قبول کرنے کا اختیار ہو تو ایجاب کرنے والے کو بہت انتظار کرنا ہوگا جس سے حرج پیدا ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں کے درمیان کی چیز مجلس کو قبول کرنے کا معیار شریعت نے رکھا۔ اس قبول کو خیار قبول کہتے ہیں (۲) اوپر کی حدیث میں حضور نے بعنیہ کہا اور حضرت عمر نے مجلس ہی میں ھو لک یا رسول اللہ کہہ کر قبول کیا، جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مجلس میں ہی قبول کرے۔ اگر مجلس کے بعد قبول کیا اور ایجاب کرنے والے نے اس کو مان لیا تب بھی بیچ ہو جائے گی کیونکہ رضامندی ہوگئی۔ خط میں اور کسی کو پیغام بھیجنے میں خط کے پہنچنے کی مجلس اور پیغام کے پہنچے کی جلس کا اعتبار ہے کہ اس مجلس میں مرسل الیہ نے قبول کر لیا تو بات طے ہو جائے گی۔ اصول مجلس تک قبول کر سکتا ہے اس کے بعد نہیں۔
When one of the contracting parties makes an offer of sale, the other has the option: if he wishes he may accept in the session, and if he wishes he may reject it. [822] That a sale will not occur without the consent of the seller and buyer, and this consent is expressed through offer and acceptance. Therefore, offer and acceptance are necessary. There is proof of this in the hadith: from Ibn Umar, he said: We were with the Prophet (PBUH) on a journey, and I was riding a difficult young camel of Umar... The Prophet said to Umar: 'Sell it to me.' He said: 'It is for you, O Messenger of Allah.' (Bukhari, chapter: If someone buys and then gifts immediately before separating, no. 2115) In this hadith, the Prophet made an offer by saying 'Sell it to me' and Umar accepted by saying 'It is for you, O Messenger of Allah.' Therefore, in a sale, offer and acceptance are necessary. Note: If the seller gives the commodity and the buyer takes it, and the price is known, but they do not make any offer and acceptance, this is a sale by mutual delivery (bai' ta'ati). This also constitutes a valid sale, because consent has occurred and it indicates offer and acceptance. [8](2) So when one of the seller and buyer makes an offer of sale, the other has the option: if he wishes he may accept in the session, and if he wishes he may reject it. Explanation: After one makes an offer of sale, the other has the option to accept it or reject it, but the option to accept is only valid as long as the session continues. If the session ends, then he no longer has the option to accept. The session, no matter how long, is characterized as a place for discussion, because if the condition to accept immediately were imposed, the acceptor would have no chance to think, and if acceptance could be done after the session, the offeror would have to wait a long time, causing hardship. Therefore, the Shari'ah has made the session the criterion for acceptance between the two. This acceptance is called khiyar al-qabul (option of acceptance). (2) In the above hadith, the Prophet said 'Sell it to me' and Umar accepted in the session by saying 'It is for you, O Messenger of Allah,' indicating that acceptance should be in the session. If acceptance occurs after the session and the offeror agrees, even then the sale takes place because consent has occurred. In the case of a letter or a message, the session of receiving the letter or the message is considered: if the recipient accepts in that session, the matter is settled. Principle: One can accept up to the session, not after.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding the option after an offer in a sale. The text establishes that when one party makes an offer (ijab), the other party has the option (khiyar) to accept or reject the offer. However, this acceptance must occur in the same sitting (majlis) as the offer. The text provides essential proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet (PBUH) made an offer and Umar accepted in the same gathering. This demonstrates the requirement of offer and acceptance for a valid sale. The note on bai' ta'ati (sale by mutual delivery) is an exception: if goods and price are exchanged without verbal offer and acceptance, the sale is still valid because actions indicate consent. The commentary explains the wisdom behind limiting acceptance to the session: immediate acceptance would give no time for thought, while delayed acceptance would cause hardship for the offeror. Therefore, the Shari'ah designates the session as the timeframe for acceptance, called khiyar al-qabul. The principle derived is that the offeree may accept only within the session; after that, the offer lapses. This ruling is from the Hanafi madhhab, specifically from the matn (likely al-Quduri) and its commentary (sharh).

Key Terms
ایجاب (ijab): The declaration of offer from the seller or buyer to initiate a sale.
قبول (qabul): The declaration of acceptance by the other party in response to the offer.
مجلس (majlis): The physical gathering or session in which the contracting parties meet and negotiate.
خیار (khiyar): The option or right to choose to accept or reject the offer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Within three days
B) At any time before the offeror revokes it
C) Only in the same session (majlis) as the offer
D) Only after physical separation of the parties

Key Takeaway
Acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer; the session defines the window for khiyar al-qabul.

Leaving the Session Before Acceptance Voids the Offer
Ruling stated with expansion on what constitutes ending the session.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that leaving the session voids the offer and identify actions that constitute implied withdrawal (i'rad).

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the session is a temporal condition — once it ends, the offer lapses.

This lesson explains a key condition in offer and acceptance: the requirement that acceptance occurs in the same session. We'll see how leaving the session or engaging in unrelated activities terminates the offer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act here is the offer (ijab). The ruling: if either party leaves the session before acceptance, the offer becomes void (batil).
2
Understand the temporal scope
The option to accept is limited to the session. Once the session ends, the offer cannot be accepted.
The session is defined by mutual presence and engagement in negotiation.
3
Recognize explicit vs implicit withdrawal
Explicit: physically standing up and leaving. Implicit (i'rad): any action indicating disinterest, such as engaging in another conversation.
The text says: 'any action that indicates turning away also ends the session.'
4
Apply to examples
Given a scenario, determine whether the offer remains valid or has been voided based on the actions of the parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فايهما قام من المجلس قبل القبول بطل الايجاب. ۸۲) (۳) بائع اومشتری مین سے جو بھی قبول سے پہلے مجلس سے اٹھ جائیں گے تو ایجاب باطل ہو جائے گا۔ چونکہ قبول کرنے کا اختیار مجلس تک ہی تھا اس لئے مجلس ختم ہونے کے بعد قبول کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا اور ایجاب ختم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مجلس سے اٹھ جانا ایجاب سے اعراض کرنے کی دلیل ہے۔ ہر وہ عمل جو اعراض پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس سے بھی مجلس ختم ہو جائے گی اور ایجاب باطل ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا ایجاب کے بعد قبول کرنے والا مجلس ہی میں کسی اور کام میں مشغول ہو گیا تو ایجاب کی مجلس ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ اعراض سے مجلس ختم ہو جاتی ہے۔
Whichever of the two leaves the session before acceptance, the offer becomes void. 82) (3) Whoever among the seller and buyer leaves the session before acceptance, then the offer becomes void. Since the option to accept was only until the session, after the session ends there is no option to accept, and the offer terminates. Because leaving the session is evidence of turning away from the offer. Any action that indicates turning away also ends the session and voids the offer. For example, after the offer, if the offeree engages in some other matter in the session itself, then the session of the offer ends. Turning away ends the session.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining the condition of the session for acceptance. The text states that if either party (seller or buyer) physically leaves the session (majlis) before acceptance takes place, then the offer (ijab) is void. The reasoning is that the option to accept is limited to the session; once the session ends, the offer lapses. Leaving the session is considered an indication of disinterest or withdrawal (i'rad). Any action that implies turning away from the negotiation also constitutes ending the session, such as the offeree engaging in another activity unrelated to the sale. This ruling ensures that both parties are actively engaged in the transaction during the session. It is a logical extension of the principle that acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer. If acceptance were allowed after departure, the offeror would be unfairly bound. Thus, the Hanafi position safeguards against indefinite suspense. This is a straightforward ruling without additional proof in the text, as it is derived from the earlier principle.

Key Terms
قام من المجلس (qama min al-majlis): To stand up and leave the session, indicating termination of the negotiation.
اعراض (i'rad): Turning away or showing disinterest, which voids the offer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The offer remains valid until the offeree returns attention
B) The offer becomes void because it indicates turning away
C) The offer is extended to the next session
D) The offer becomes binding on both parties

Key Takeaway
Leaving the session or any action indicating disinterest voids the offer; acceptance must occur in the same session.

Binding Nature of Sale After Acceptance and the Option of Session Dispute
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on khiyar al-majlis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on khiyar al-majlis and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the interpretation of 'tafarruq'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, acceptance ends the option of session; the sale is binding immediately.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on khiyar al-majlis. The Hanafi ruling that a sale becomes binding immediately upon acceptance, with no further option of the session, is grounded in a specific interpretation of the prophetic hadith. We will explore the linguistic analysis and the practical implications of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that once offer and acceptance are exchanged, the sale is binding (lazim) and no party can rescind it based on khiyar al-majlis.
The exception of defect or sight remains.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the option continues until the parties physically separate, based on the same hadith.
This is the core of the dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith of Hakim ibn Hizam and the interpretation of 'tafarruq' as verbal acceptance, supported by Umar and Sufyan.
Linguistic analysis is key.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafis argue that once acceptance occurs, the parties are no longer 'mutabayi'an' (two persons negotiating a sale) and thus the hadith's option no longer applies.
This refutes the Shafi'i literal reading.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in Hanafi, a buyer cannot rescind after saying 'I accept' even if still in the shop; in Shafi'i, he can until leaving the session.
Affects contract stability and business practice.

Source Text

ہاں ! مبیع میں عیب ہو یا مبیع کو دیکھا نہ ہو تو خیار عیب اور خیار رویت کی وجہ سے بیع توڑنے کی اجازت ہوگی ۔ مجلس باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے خیار مجلس کی بنیاد پر بیع توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا، یعنی حنفیہ کے نزدیک خیار مجلس کسی کو نہیں ہوگا ۔ حدیث میں عن حكيم بن حزام قال قال رسول الله البيعان بالخيار مالم يتفرقا (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذابین البيعان ولم يكتما نصحا ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۲۰۷۹ ر مسلم شریف، باب ثبوت خیار مجلس للمتها یعین ج ثانی ص ۳۱ نمبر ۱۵۳۱ر ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۳۴۵۹ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۲۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بائع اور مشتری کو بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہو گا جب تک تفرق نہ کرے یعنی قبول نہ کرے۔ تفرق کا ترجمہ قبول کرنا اور بات پر بات جمانا ہے۔ جب ایجاب کے بعد قبول کر لیا تو بیع مستحکم ہوگئی اب توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا چاہے بیع کی مجلس بر قرار ہو۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے تفرق کی یہی تفسیر کی ہے وقال عمر البيع عن صفقة او خيار (ب) مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب البيان بالخيار مالم فر تاج ثامن ص ۵۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۷۴ار مصنف ابن ابی همته ۳۷۹ من کان یوجب البیع از اتكلم به ، ج رابغ ص ۵۰۷ نمبر ۲۲۵۶۹) حضرت سفیان نے بھی تفرق کی یہی تغیر کی ہے قال سفيان والصقة باللسان (ج) مصنف عبد الرزاق ج ثامن ص ۵۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۷۳) کہ بیج زبان سے طے ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں المتبايعان (بیع کرنے والے) ہے۔ اور بیچ کرنے والے اس وقت کہے جاتے ہیں جب ایجاب اور قبول کر رہے ہوں۔ اور اسی حالت میں ان کو نہ قبول کرنے کا یا قبول سے پہلے ایجاب کرنے والے کو اپنی بات واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اور جب قبول کر لیا تو متبایجان کی صفت ختم ہو گئی اس لئے حدیث کی رو سے رابع ، ص ۵۰۶، نمبر ۲۲۵۶۰) امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ قبول کرنے کے بعد اور بیع مکمل ہونے کے بعد بھی مجلس بھیج موجود ہوتو دونوں کو اپنی اپنی بات واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ حاشیہ: (الف) آپ نے فرمایا بائع اور مشتری کو اختیار ہے جب قول کا تفرق نہ ہو یعنی قبول نہ کر لے یا جب تک دونوں جدا نہ ہوں (ب) حضرت عمر نے فرمایا بیچ صفقہ سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے یعنی قبول کرنے سے، پانچ کو اختیار کرنے سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے (ج) حضرت سفیان نے فرمایا زبان سے ملحقہ ہو تو بیچ پوری ہو جائے گی۔
When offer and acceptance occur, the sale becomes binding, and neither party has an option except for a defect or [not having seen]. Explanation: Both seller and buyer have made offer and acceptance, now the sale is complete. Even if the session is still ongoing, no one has the right to break the sale. However, if there is a defect in the commodity or if the commodity was not seen, then due to khiyar al-ayb (option of defect) and khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight), breaking the sale is permitted. There is no right to break the sale due to khiyar al-majlis (option of session) based on the session continuing, meaning according to the Hanafis no one has khiyar al-majlis. In the hadith: from Hakim ibn Hizam, he said: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they do not separate (tafarraqa).' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) In this hadith, the seller and buyer have the option to break the sale as long as tafarrq does not occur, meaning as long as acceptance does not occur. The translation of tafarrq is acceptance and settling the matter firmly. When acceptance occurs after the offer, the sale becomes binding; now there is no option to break it even if the sale session is ongoing. Umar (RA) interpreted tafarrq in this way: 'The sale is completed by a binding agreement or option.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) Sufyan also interpreted tafarrq in this way: 'The sale is completed by the tongue.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) (2) In the hadith, the word 'al-mutabayi'an' (the two parties in a sale) refers to those who are in the process of offering and accepting. In that state, they have the option not to accept, or the offeror has the option to withdraw his statement before acceptance. When acceptance occurs, the description of mutabayi'an ends; therefore, based on the hadith, they no longer have the option to withdraw. Another hadith: from Abu Dharr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they do not separate from their sale.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) Imam Shafi'i and other imams opine that after acceptance and completion of the sale, if the session is still ongoing, both parties still have the option to withdraw their statements. Footnotes: (a) He said: The seller and buyer have the option as long as the words do not separate, i.e., as long as acceptance does not occur, or as long as they are not physically separated. (b) Umar said: The sale is completed by a binding agreement or option. (c) Sufyan said: When it is concluded by the tongue, the sale is complete.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a ruling statement and an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling is that once offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) have been exchanged, the sale contract is binding (lazim) and neither party has any option to rescind it, except for specific rights like khiyar al-ayb (option for defect) or khiyar al-ru'yah (option for not having seen the object). The commentary explicitly states that according to the Hanafi madhhab, there is no khiyar al-majlis (option of the session) after the contract is concluded. The text then addresses the famous hadith of Hakim ibn Hizam: 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they do not separate (ma lam yatafarraqa).' The Hanafi interpretation explains that 'tafarruq' here means separation by acceptance or verbal agreement, not physical separation. Thus, once acceptance is pronounced, the contract is final and no option remains. The passage cites the interpretations of Umar ibn al-Khattab and Sufyan al-Thawri supporting this view. It then contrasts with the position of Imam al-Shafi'i and other scholars who hold that the option of the session continues until the parties physically separate, even after verbal acceptance. This difference leads to practical consequences: in the Hanafi school, the sale is immediately binding upon acceptance; in the Shafi'i school, either party may still rescind as long as they remain in the same place. The Hanafi position relies on understanding 'tafarruq' as completion of the contract by mutual consent, not physical departure. This passage demonstrates how a single hadith can be interpreted differently, leading to divergent rulings in Islamic law.

Key Terms
خیار مجلس (khiyar al-majlis): The option to rescind a sale contract as long as the parties remain in the same session after the contract is concluded.
تفرق (tafarruq): In this context, separation of the parties by acceptance/agreement (Hanafi view) or by physical departure (Shafi'i view).
لازم (lazim): Binding; a contract that cannot be unilaterally rescinded without a recognized defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when does the option to rescind a sale (khiyar al-majlis) end?
A) When the parties physically leave the meeting place
B) When the buyer has paid the full price
C) When the seller has delivered the goods
D) When offer and acceptance are verbally concluded

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, khiyar al-majlis ends with verbal acceptance; the sale becomes binding immediately, unlike the Shafi'i view.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Khiyar al-Majlis: Hanafi Refutation and Hadith Interpretation
Hanafi refutation of khiyar al-majlis with hadith interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-majlis, explain the Hanafi interpretation of the relevant hadith, and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Once offer and acceptance are exchanged, the sale is binding; no khiyar al-majlis.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a buyer or seller have the right to rescind a sale while still in the same session after offer and acceptance? The Hanafi school firmly rejects khiyar al-majlis, while the Shafi'i school upholds it. The key lies in the interpretation of a single prophetic hadith. Let's walk through the Hanafi argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: once offer and acceptance occur, the sale is binding and no party has an option to rescind based on the session alone.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school (and others) hold that khiyar al-majlis exists until the parties physically separate, even after acceptance.
The same hadith is the basis for both positions.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The hadith 'al-bayyi'ani bi al-khiyar ma lam yatafarraqa' is interpreted by Shafi'is as physical separation.
They also rely on the practice of Ibn Umar who would walk away after purchase.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret 'tafarruq' as verbal separation (acceptance), supported by narrations from Umar and Sufyan. Also, the term 'al-mutabayi'an' applies only during the exchange of offer/acceptance.
The Hanafi response is both linguistic and contextual.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis do not allow rescission after acceptance; Shafi'is allow it until physical departure.
This difference affects real-world transactions, including modern online sales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
[۲۳] (۴) فاذا حصل الايجاب والقبول لزم البيع ولا خيار لواحد منهما الا من عيب او عدم روية [۸۲۴] (۵)

اٹھ جانا ایجاب سے اعراض کرنے کی دلیل ہے۔ ہر وہ عمل جو اعراض پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس سے بھی مجلس ختم ہو جائے گی اور ایجاب باطل ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا ایجاب کے بعد قبول کرنے والا مجلس ہی میں کسی اور کام میں مشغول ہو گیا تو ایجاب کی مجلس ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ اعراض سے مجلس ختم ہو جاتی ہے۔

۸۲۳] (۴) پس جب ایجاب اور قبول حاصل ہو جائے تو بیع لازم ہو جائے گی اور بائع اور مشتری دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو اختیار نہیں ہوگا ۔ مگر عیب اور نہ دیکھنے کی وجہ سے۔ شرح بائع اور مشتری دونوں نے ایجاب قبول کر لئے اب بیع مکمل ہو گئی۔ چاہے مجلس موجود ہو پھر بھی کسی کو بیع توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے ہاں ! مبیع میں عیب ہو یا مبیع کو دیکھا نہ ہو تو خیار عیب اور خیار رویت کی وجہ سے بیع توڑنے کی اجازت ہوگی ۔ مجلس باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے خیار مجلس کی بنیاد پر بیع توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا، یعنی حنفیہ کے نزدیک خیار مجلس کسی کو نہیں ہوگا ۔

حدیث میں عن حكيم بن حزام قال قال رسول الله البيعان بالخيار مالم يتفرقا (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذابین البيعان ولم يكتما نصحا ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۲۰۷۹ ر مسلم شریف، باب ثبوت خیار مجلس للمتها یعین ج ثانی ص ۳۱ نمبر ۱۵۳۱ر ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۳۴۵۹ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۲۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بائع اور مشتری کو بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہو گا جب تک تفرق نہ کرے یعنی قبول نہ کرے۔ تفرق کا ترجمہ قبول کرنا اور بات پر بات جمانا ہے۔ جب ایجاب کے بعد قبول کر لیا تو بیع مستحکم ہوگئی اب توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا چاہے بیع کی مجلس بر قرار ہو۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے تفرق کی یہی تفسیر کی ہے وقال عمر البيع عن صفقة او خيار (ب) مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب البيان بالخيار مالم فر تاج ثامن ص ۵۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۷۴ار مصنف ابن ابی همته ۳۷۹ من كان یوجب البیع از اتكلم به ، ج رابغ ص ۵۰۷ نمبر ۲۲۵۶۹) حضرت سفیان نے بھی تفرق کی یہی تغیر کی ہے قال سفيان والصقة باللسان (ج) مصنف عبد الرزاق ج ثامن ص ۵۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۷۳) کہ بیج زبان سے طے ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں المتبايعان (بیع کرنے والے) ہے۔ اور بیچ کرنے والے اس وقت کہے جاتے ہیں جب ایجاب اور قبول کر رہے ہوں۔ اور اسی حالت میں ان کو نہ قبول کرنے کا یا قبول سے پہلے ایجاب کرنے والے کو اپنی بات واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اور جب قبول کر لیا تو متبایجان کی صفت ختم ہو گئی اس لئے حدیث کی رو سے اب ان کو بات واپس لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ عن ابی زیر قال قال رسول الله الا الله البيعان بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا من بيعهما (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۳۷۸ من قال البيعان بالخيار مالم يغر قاج رابع ، ص ۵۰۶، نمبر ۲۲۵۶۰) امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ قبول کرنے کے بعد اور بیع مکمل ہونے کے بعد بھی مجلس بھیج موجود ہوتو دونوں کو اپنی اپنی بات واپس
حاشیہ: (الف) آپ نے فرمایا بائع اور مشتری کو اختیار ہے جب قول کا تفرق نہ ہو یعنی قبول نہ کر لے یا جب تک دونوں جدا نہ ہوں (ب) حضرت عمر نے فرمایا بیچ صفقہ
سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے یعنی قبول کرنے سے، پانچ کو اختیار کرنے سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے (ج) حضرت سفیان نے فرمایا زبان سے ملحقہ ہو تو بیچ پوری ہو جائے گی۔

عدم رؤية [۸۲۴](۵) والاعواض المشار اليها لا يحتاج الى معرفة مقدارها في جواز لینے اور بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا اور دونوں کو خیار مجلس ہوگا۔
The book of sales. [23] (4) So when offer and acceptance occur, the sale becomes binding, and neither party has an option except due to defect or lack of sight. [824] (5)

Getting up is evidence of turning away from the offer. Every action that indicates turning away will also end the session and the offer becomes void. For example, after the offer, the acceptor engages in another matter in the session itself, then the session of the offer ends. The session ends by turning away.

[823] (4) So when offer and acceptance are obtained, the sale becomes binding, and neither the seller nor the buyer has an option except due to defect or non-sight. Explanation: The seller and buyer have both made offer and acceptance; now the sale is complete. Even if the session continues, still no one has the right to break the sale. Yes! If there is a defect in the sold item or it was not seen, then due to the option of defect and option of sight, breaking the sale is permitted. Due to the continuation of the session, there is no right to break the sale based on the option of the session; that is, according to the Hanafis, no one has the option of the session.

In a hadith: From Hakim ibn Hizam, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they have not separated' (a) (Bukhari, Bab idha tabaya'a al-bay'ani wa lam yaktuma nushaha, p. 279, no. 2079; Muslim, Bab thubut khiyar al-majlis li al-mutabayi'ayn, vol. 2, p. 31, no. 1531; Abu Dawud no. 3459; Tirmidhi no. 1246). In this hadith, it is that the seller and buyer have the option to break the sale as long as they have not made tafarruq, i.e., acceptance. The translation of tafarruq is to accept and settle the matter. When acceptance is made after the offer, the sale is strengthened; now there is no option to break, even if the session of the sale continues. Hadrat Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) gave the same interpretation of tafarruq and said: 'The sale is [settled] by a transaction or by an option' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-bay'ani bi al-khiyar ma lam yatafarraqa, vol. 8, p. 53, no. 14274; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 379, man kana yujibu al-bay'a idha takallama bihi, vol. 4, p. 507, no. 22569). Hadrat Sufyan also gave the same interpretation of tafarruq: he said: 'And the transaction is by the tongue' (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 8, p. 53, no. 14273) that the sale is settled by the tongue. (2) In the hadith, 'al-mutabayi'an' (the two parties in a sale) is mentioned. And they are called parties in a sale when they are making offer and acceptance. And in that state, they have the option to not accept or, before acceptance, the offerer may withdraw his statement. And when acceptance is made, the quality of being parties in a sale ceases, so according to the hadith, they no longer have the option to withdraw. In another hadith: From Abi Dharr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the two parties in a sale have the option as long as they have not separated from their sale' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 378, man qala al-bayi'ani bi al-khiyar ma lam yatafarraqa, vol. 4, p. 506, no. 22560). Imam Shafi'i and other imams are of the opinion that after acceptance and completion of the sale, if the session continues, both have the option to withdraw their statements.

Footnote: (a) He said: The seller and buyer have the option when there is no separation of speech, i.e., acceptance has not occurred, or as long as both have not physically separated. (b) Hadrat Umar said: The sale is complete by the transaction, i.e., by acceptance, by choosing the fifth. (c) Hadrat Sufyan said: When the conjunction occurs by the tongue, the sale becomes complete.

Non-sight [824] (5) And the countervalues pointed to do not require knowledge of their quantity for permissibility.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and other schools (especially Shafi'is) regarding the option of the session (khiyar al-majlis). The text begins by stating the Hanafi position: once offer and acceptance are exchanged, the sale is binding and no party has an option to rescind based on the continuing session; only options for defect or non-sight remain. The commentator provides Hanafi reasoning: getting up or engaging in another act indicates turning away from the offer, ending the session. Then the hadith of Hakim ibn Hizam is cited, which says the parties have an option as long as they have not separated (tafarruq). The Hanafis interpret 'tafarruq' as separation through acceptance (verbal settlement), not physical separation. Evidence from the actions of Umar and Sufyan is given. The Shafi'i view is then presented: they interpret tafarruq as physical separation, thus khiyar al-majlis exists even after acceptance as long as the session continues. The Hanafi response is implicit in the interpretation and in the claim that the parties are called 'al-mutabayi'an' only while making offer/acceptance, so after acceptance they are no longer within the scope of the hadith. The footnote supports the Hanafi interpretation.

Key Terms
خیار المجلس (Khiyar al-Majlis): The option to rescind a sale while the contracting parties are still in the same session before they physically separate.
تفرق (Tafarruq): Separation; in this context, Hanafis interpret it as separation of speech (acceptance) while Shafi'is interpret it as physical separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what terminates the option period in a sale?
A) Physical separation of the parties
B) The passing of a specific time
C) Completion of offer and acceptance
D) Inspection of the goods

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not recognize khiyar al-majlis because it interprets the hadith's 'tafarruq' as verbal acceptance, making the sale binding immediately upon offer and acceptance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling by Pointing: No Quantity Knowledge Needed
Ruling that knowledge of quantity is unnecessary when commodity is present and pointed to

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a present commodity by pointing and apply it to distinguish sales of present goods from sales of absent goods.

Core Idea
If the commodity is present and seen, the sale is valid without specifying the exact quantity.

Have you ever wondered whether you can buy a pile of apples just by pointing and agreeing on a price, without weighing them? In Hanafi fiqh, when the item is right in front of you and the sale is concluded by pointing, the contract is valid even if you don't know the exact weight or count. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states: when the countervalues (item and price) are present and pointed to at the time of sale, knowledge of their quantity is not required for validity. This applies to both the sold commodity and the price.
The ruling is specific to present goods, not absent ones.
2
Understand the first proof: mutual consent
The hadith 'لا يفترقن اثنان إلا عن تراض' is cited. The Hanafi reasoning: since the buyer sees the item and agrees, the sale is valid, and no further specification of quantity is needed.
The dalal (implication) from mutual consent supports waiver of precise quantification.
3
Analyze the second proof: jizaf (bulk sale)
The hadith from Ibn Umar shows that people in the Prophet's time bought food in bulk (jizaf) without precise measurement. This establishes the permissibility of selling present goods by estimation.
Jizaf means sale by estimation, allowed when the goods are visible.
4
Contrast with absent goods
The text explicitly notes that for absent goods, quantity and description must be specified. Present goods are exempt because sight substitutes for description.
This distinction is crucial: present goods require only sight and pointing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدم رؤية [۸۲۴](۵) والاعواض المشار اليها لا يحتاج الى معرفة مقدارها في جواز لینے اور بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا اور دونوں کو خیار مجلس ہوگا۔

۸۲۴۱] (۵) بدلے کی چیز جس کی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہو بیچ کے جائز ہونے میں اس کی مقدار پہچاننے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ الاعواض سے مراد ہے مبیع یا شمن جو بدلے میں دیئے جاتے ہیں۔ اگر مبیع یا شمن سامنے موجود ہوا اور بیچ کے وقت اس کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا ہو تو اس کی مقدار کتنی ہے، کتنے کیلو ہے یا کتنی تعداد ہے بیچ کے جائز ہونے میں اس کو جانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس کے متعین کئے بغیر بھی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔

پچھلے زمانے میں کوئی چیز سامنے ہو تو اس کی مقدار جانے بغیر بیچ کر لیا کرتے تھے۔ کیونکہ مشتری اس کو اسی حال میں خریدنے کے لئے راضی ہے۔ اور جہاں تک اچھا یا خراب ہونے کی بات ہے تو مشتری خود اس کو آنکھوں سے دیکھ کر خرید رہا ہے اور اس پر راضی ہے۔ اس لئے بیچ ہو جائے گی حدیث میں ہے سمعت ابا هريرة يقول قال رسول الله الا الله لا يفترقن اثنان الا عن تراض (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی خیار المتبایعین ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۴۵۸) معلوم ہوا کہ چیز سامنے ہو اور رضامندی سے خرید رہا ہو تو بیع جائز ہے۔ انکل سے بیچ بیچنے کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے ان ابن عمر قال رايت الناس في عهد رسول الله الله يبتاعون جزافا يعنى الطعام ( ج ) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من رای اذا اشترى طعاما جزافا ص ۲۸۶ نمبر ۲۱۳۷ ر مسلم شریف ، باب بطلان بيع السميع قبل القبض ج ثانی ص ۵ نمبر ۱۵۲۷/ ۳۸۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مبیع سامنے ہو تو انکل سے بیچ سکتا ہے چاہے مقدار کا پتہ نہ ہو۔

انوان بیع کے لئے غائب چیز کی مقدار اور صفت بیان کی جاتی ہے۔ موجود کی نہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت نافع فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر جب کسی سے بیچ کرنے اور اقالہ کرتے کی نیت نہ ہوتی تو کھڑے ہو کر چلتے پھر واپس لوٹ آتے تا کہ خیار مجلس سے بیچ تو ڑ نہ دے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا دونوں آدمی جدا نہ ہوں مگر رضامندی کے ساتھ (ج) عبد اللہ ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے لوگوں کو حضور کے زمانے میں دیکھا وہ نملوں کو انکل سے بیچتے تھے۔
Non-sight [824] (5) And the countervalues pointed to do not require knowledge of their quantity for permissibility. And ... [Urdu: and they will have the option to take and break the sale, and both will have the option of the session.]

[8241] (5) The thing given in exchange which has been pointed to, knowledge of its quantity is not necessary for the validity of the sale. 'Al-a'wad' means the sold commodity or the price which are given in exchange. If the sold commodity or price is present in front and at the time of sale it is pointed to, then it is not necessary to know its quantity, how many kilograms or how many in number, for the validity of the sale. Without specifying it, the sale becomes valid.

In earlier times, if something was in front, they would buy and sell without knowing its quantity. Because the buyer is satisfied to buy it in that state. And as for goodness or badness, the buyer himself is seeing it with his eyes and is satisfied with it. Therefore the sale takes place. In a hadith: I heard Abu Huraira say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, two persons do not separate except with mutual consent' (b) (Abu Dawud, Bab fi khiyar al-mutabayi'ayn, vol. 2, p. 133, no. 3458). It became clear that if the thing is in front and he is buying with satisfaction, then the sale is valid. The evidence for selling in bulk (jizafan) is in a hadith: Ibn Umar said: I saw people in the time of the Messenger of Allah buying food in bulk (i.e., grain) (c) (Bukhari, Bab man ra'a idha ishtara ta'aman jizafan, p. 286, no. 2137; Muslim, Bab butlan bay' al-sam'i qabla al-qabd, vol. 2, p. 5, no. 1527/3847). From this hadith, it became clear that if the sold commodity is present, one can sell in bulk even if the quantity is not known.

For the sale of absent goods, the quantity and description are given; for present goods, not.

Footnote: (a) Hadrat Nafi' says: Hadrat Abdullah ibn Umar, when he would make a sale and did not intend to revoke it, would stand up, walk a bit, then return to him, so that he would not break the sale due to the option of the session. (b) He said: 'Two persons do not separate except with mutual consent.' (c) Abdullah ibn Umar says: I saw people in the time of the Prophet buying in bulk, i.e., food.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of selling a present commodity by pointing (i.e., without specifying exact quantity). The text first states the rule: when the countervalues (commodity or price) are present and pointed to, knowledge of their exact quantity is not necessary for the validity of the sale. The commentator explains that if the item is physically present, the buyer is satisfied with it as seen, and it is not required to specify the exact weight or count. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Abu Huraira that the two parties should not separate except with mutual consent—this implies that as long as both parties are satisfied, the sale is valid, even without quantifying. (2) The hadith of Ibn Umar that people in the Prophet's time bought and sold food in bulk (jizafan), meaning by estimation without precise measurement. This establishes the permissibility of selling present goods in bulk. The text contrasts this with the sale of absent goods, where description of quantity and quality is required.

Key Terms
جُزاف (Jizaf): Buying or selling in bulk without exact measurement or weighing, relying on estimation.
الاعواض المشار إليها (Al-A'wad al-Musharu Ilayha): The countervalues (item and price) that are physically present and pointed to at the time of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to sell a commodity without specifying its exact quantity in Hanafi fiqh?
A) When the commodity is absent
B) When the buyer trusts the seller
C) When the commodity is present and pointed to
D) When the price is very low

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sale by pointing at a present commodity is valid and does not require knowledge of exact quantity because the buyer's sight and consent replace precise specification.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Absolute Price Must Be Known in Quantity and Quality
Ruling on the invalidity of absolute price without specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with an unspecified price and identify the proofs from the Sunnah that support it.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the price or item is unknown in quantity and quality — uncertainty in the essential term voids the contract.

In this lesson, we examine a core principle of Hanafi sales law: the price must be clearly specified at the time of contract. The passage presents three hadith proofs that establish this requirement, drawing from the rules of salam, the prohibition of gharar, and the ban on selling unborn animals. Understanding this principle helps you avoid contracts that are fasid due to jahalah (ignorance).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage begins with the ruling: absolute prices (al-thaman al-mutlaq) are not valid unless their quantity (kayl, wazn, or 'adad) and quality (sifah) are known. An absolute price is one that is absent or not pointed to, with unknown measure and quality.
This applies to both the price and the sold item in a deferred or absent transaction.
2
Examine the First Proof: Hadith of Salam
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be with a known measure, known weight, and known term.' This shows that for a future delivery, specification is obligatory. By analogy, any absent or deferred price must also be specified.
The command 'ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم' indicates obligation (wujub).
3
Examine the Second Proof: Prohibition of Gharar
The hadith forbids 'bay' al-gharar' (the sale of deceit). An unspecified price is a form of gharar because it leads to uncertainty and potential dispute. Therefore, such a sale is prohibited.
Gharar is any transaction where the subject matter or consideration is unknown to one or both parties.
4
Examine the Third Proof: Prohibition of Selling the Unborn
The sale of habal al-habalah (the fetus in the womb) is forbidden because its quantity and quality are unknown. This analogy extends to any absent price whose specifications are unknown.
This reinforces the principle that jahalah in the price renders the sale invalid.
5
Synthesize the Principle
The common theme from all proofs is that a sale with an unspecified price is invalid due to gharar. The Hanafi school therefore requires the price to be known in quantity and quality at the time of contract.
If the price is subsequently agreed upon, the sale may be rectified, but initially it is fasid (voidable).

(6) Absolute prices are not valid unless they are known in quantity. The term 'al-a'rad' is the plural of 'iwad, meaning a thing given in exchange; here it refers to the sold item or the price. (6) And a sale with an absolute price is not valid unless its quantity and quality are known. That price which is not present but absent and not pointed to—its quantity, e.g., how many kilos or litres, and its quality, e.g., good or bad, is not known—a sale with it is not permissible until that is known. Because the seller cannot see the absent item to express consent, so there is deception in it. Therefore, sale with it is not permissible. In the hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet came to Madinah and they used to sell fruits in advance for two or three years. So he said: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be with a known measure, known weight, and known term.' (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith, it is understood that when the thing being sold is not present, its measure or weight and term must be known for the sale to be valid, otherwise not. (2) A sale without consent is not permissible; its proof was in the hadith of Abu Hurairah, number 3358. (3) And a sale involving deception is not permissible; its proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'The Prophet forbade the sale by throwing stones and the sale of gharar (deception).' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this, it is understood that any sale involving deception is not permissible. And a sale of an unknown thing is not permissible; its proof is the hadith of Abdullah: 'The Prophet forbade the sale of the fetus in the womb (habal al-habalah).' (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, the fetus inside the animal cannot be seen; its quality is unknown and its quantity is unknown, so it was deemed impermissible to sell it. From this it is understood that it is not permissible to sell or buy an absent thing whose quantity and quality are not known. Principle: For an absent price, specifying its quantity and quality is necessary. (2) A deceptive thing can be neither the sold item nor the price. 'Al-athman al-mutlaqah' means the price that is absent or whose quantity and quality are not known. 'Al-qadr' means quantity, e.g., how many kilos.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs. It states the general principle that a price (or the sold item) that is not specified in quantity and quality renders the sale invalid. The commentary explains the term 'al-athman al-mutlaqah' (absolute prices) and provides three hadith proofs: (1) The hadith of Salam (advance payment) requiring known measure, weight, and term; (2) The hadith on the necessity of mutual consent; (3) The prohibition of gharar (deceptive transactions) and the prohibition of selling the unborn animal. The underlying reason is the elimination of jahalah (ignorance) which leads to dispute. The commentator reiterates that the quantity and quality of an absent price must be specified.

Key Terms
الثمن المطلق (al-thaman al-mutlaq): A price that is not specified by quantity or quality, or is absent without being pointed to.
الغرر (al-gharar): Deception or uncertainty in a transaction that may lead to dispute.

Sale with Immediate or Deferred Price Requires Known Term
Ruling on validity of cash and credit sales with known term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cash and credit sales and explain the requirement of a known term using the Quranic and Prophetic proofs.

Core Idea
Both cash and credit sales are valid, but the term must be known to avoid dispute.

This lesson establishes the basic permissibility of selling for cash or on credit. The Hanafi school, relying on the general Quranic permission of trade and the Prophet's own practice, holds that as long as the payment term is clearly defined, the sale is valid. The key is certainty: an unknown term leads to potential conflict and invalidates the sale.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the rule
Read the first sentence: 'It is permissible to sell with a prompt price and a deferred price when the term is known.' This is the ruling.
Note that both cash and credit are equally valid.
2
Identify the condition
The condition for a credit sale is that the term (ajal) must be known. The text explains why: an unknown term leads to delay and dispute.
The term refers to the specific date or period for payment.
3
Locate the primary proof
The first proof is the Quranic verse 'Ahalla Allah al-bay‘' (Allah has permitted trade). The commentator argues this is general, encompassing both cash and credit.
The verse does not restrict to any particular type of sale.
4
Locate the secondary proof
The second proof is the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit, pledging his armor. This shows the permissibility in practice.
This hadith is cited to support the permissibility of deferred payment.
5
Confirm the consequence
If the term is known, the sale is valid and disputes avoided. If unknown, the sale is invalid because it leads to uncertainty (gharar).
Certainty in the term is essential for the validity of a credit sale.

(7) And it is permissible to sell with a prompt price and a deferred price when the term is known. Sale with cash price is permissible, and with deferred price also, provided the date is specified. If the date of payment is not specified, the buyer will delay and dispute. So at the time of sale, specify the date of payment. (2) Both types are permissible because the verse says absolutely about selling: 'But Allah has permitted trade' (Surah al-Baqarah 2). Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs. It establishes that sale can be either cash (hāl) or credit (mu’ajjal) as long as the term (ajal) is known. The proof is the general permission in the Quran for trade and the sunnah of the Prophet buying on credit. The commentator emphasizes that specifying the term is essential to avoid dispute. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse 'Ahalla allahu al-bay‘' (Allah has permitted trade), indicating that both cash and credit are permissible without distinction.

Key Terms

ثمن مؤجل (thaman mu’ajjal): Price deferred to a future date (credit price).
الاجل (al-ajal): The fixed term or deadline for payment in a credit sale.

Absolute Price Defaults to Prevalent Currency
Ruling on default currency when price is left absolute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an absolute price defaults to the prevalent currency of the locality and identify when the sale is invalid due to jahalah.

Core Idea
An absolute price is interpreted by custom: valid if one currency is predominant, invalid if equal prevalence causes uncertainty.

In Islamic law, a sale requires a known price. But what if the parties simply say 'I sell this for one hundred' without specifying the currency? The Hanafi school looks to the prevalent custom of the locality to resolve the ambiguity, provided it does not lead to dispute. This lesson explores the conditions under which such a sale is valid or invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale where the price is left absolute (no currency specified). The ruling: it is valid if it defaults to the prevalent currency.
2
Determine the condition for validity
The condition is that there must be a clear, predominant currency in the locality. If none or equal, the sale is invalid.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario A: one currency is predominant → valid. Scenario B: multiple currencies equally prevalent but different values → invalid due to jahalah.
4
Note the underlying principle
The principle is that custom ('urf) determines the meaning of absolute terms in contracts.
5
Apply to a new scenario
For example, if in a city both Saudi Riyal and Qatari Riyal are used but 'Riyal' is ambiguous, the ruling depends on which is more common.

Source Text

[۸۲۷] (۸) اطلق الثمن في البيع كان على غالب نقد البلد فان كانت النقود مختلفة يبين احدها
میں شمن مطلق رکھا تو وہ شہر کے غالب نقد پر ہوگا۔ پس اگر نقود مختلف ہوں تو بیع فاسد ہوگی مگر یہ کہ ایک نقد کو بیان
ر میں ان کے رائج ہوں اور بیچ کرتے وقت کسی ایک کو متعین نہیں کیا تو اگر کسی ایک سکے کا رواج زیادہ ہو تو وہی سکہ مراد ہوگا۔ کیونک رج زیادہ ہوتا ہے بیچ کرتے وقت دونوں کا ذہن اسی طرف جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہی مراد ہوگا اور بیع جائز ہو جائے گی لیکن اگر رواج برابر ہے اور ہر ایک کی مالیت مختلف ہے تو اب جہالت کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ بائع اعلی سکہ طلب کرے گا اور نہ دینا چاہے گا ۔ اور کوئی سکہ متعین نہیں ہے اس لئے نزاع ہوگا۔ اس لئے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ البتہ اگر مجلس ختم کی نشان دہی کر دی جائے تو وہی سکہ متعین ہو کر بیع جائز ہو جائے۔

If the price is left absolute in a sale, it is upon the prevalent currency of the place. So if the currencies are different, the sale is invalid unless one is specified. He said: When the price is left absolute, it will be upon the prevalent currency of the city. So if the currencies are different, the sale will be invalid unless one currency is specified. For example, if there are two currencies in circulation and at the time of sale neither is specified, then if one coin is more prevalent, that coin will be intended because use is more; the minds of both go towards it. Therefore, it will be intended and the sale becomes valid. But if the prevalence is equal and the value of each is different, then due to ignorance the sale becomes invalid. Because the seller will demand the higher coin and the buyer will not want to give it, and since no coin is specified, dispute will arise. So the sale becomes invalid. However, if the session ends with some indication, then that coin becomes specified and the sale becomes valid. Principle: The custom of the locality is to be considered.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. It addresses the situation where the price is left absolute (without specifying the currency) in a sale. The Hanafi position is that the price defaults to the prevailing currency of that locality. If there are multiple currencies in circulation, the sale is valid only if one currency is clearly predominant. If two currencies are equally prevalent but of unequal value, the sale is invalid due to jahalah (ignorance) that leads to dispute. The commentator also notes that if during the session the parties indicate one currency, that specification is effective. The underlying principle is that the custom of the place ('urf) is given weight.

Key Terms
غالب نقد البلد (ghālib naqd al-balad): The prevailing currency of the locality, used as default when price is absolute.
جهالت (jahālah): Ignorance about the price leading to uncertainty and dispute, invalidating the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The sale is valid and the buyer chooses the cheaper
B) The sale is invalid due to ignorance
C) The sale is valid and the seller chooses the higher
D) The sale is valid and the market price is used

Key Takeaway
An absolute price defaults to the prevalent currency of the locality, but if multiple currencies are equally common and of different values, the sale is invalid due to uncertainty.

Selling Food and Grains by Volume, Weight, and Specified Container
Ruling on valid methods for selling food and grains

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four valid methods for selling food and grains and explain why each removes uncertainty.

Core Idea
Four valid methods remove uncertainty: measure, weight, known vessel, known stone.

In Islamic commercial law, uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter of sale invalidates the contract—especially for food and grains where precise quantity matters. This passage from a classical Hanafi text lists the four acceptable methods to specify quantity: by volume, by weight, using a known container, or using a known stone (weight). Understanding these methods helps you apply the principle that knowledge of quantity is a condition for valid sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Permissible Methods
List the four methods mentioned: by measure (kayl), by weight (wazn), by a known vessel (āniyah ma'lūmah), and by a known stone (hajar ma'lūm). Note that the vessel or stone must have a known capacity or weight by custom or agreement.
These are the only ways to sell food and grains without falling into jahalah.
2
Understand Why Each Method Removes Uncertainty
Each method provides an objective standard—either through a standard unit (liter, kilogram) or through a mutually recognized container/stone. The key is that the quantity is made known at the time of contract.
Uncertainty (gharar) in quantity is a cause for prohibition.
3
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Consider: A farmer sells wheat using a container that both parties agree holds 5 kg, even though the container's exact capacity is not universally standardized. The sale is valid because the parties have agreed on a known measure.
The 'known vessel' need not be a standard official measure; mutual knowledge suffices.

Source Text

[۸۲۸] ((۹) ويجوز بيع الطعام والحبوب كلها مكائلة و موزونة و في آنية معلومة و بحجر معلوم
کے کھانے اور غلوں سب کو بیچنا کیل کر کے اور انکل سے اور متعین برتن سے جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو یا متعین پتھر کے وزن سے جس کی مقدار و علائم نہ ہو۔ جو میچ کے موجود ہو اور غلہ اور کھانے کی جنس سے ہو، درہم اور دنا نیر نہ ہوں تو اس کو چار طریقوں سے بیچنا جائز ہے جن کا تذکرہ متن میں ہے میں ان کے بیچے (۲) الکل سے ویسے ہی بیچ دے یہ بھی جائز ہے (۳) ایک برتن ہے جس کا وزن یا کیل معلوم نہیں ہے کہ اس میں کیسے کیوں کے ہیں لیکن بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان یہ طے ہو گیا کہ ایک برتن کے بدلے پانچ پونڈ دوں گا تو بیع جائز ہو جائے
It is permissible to sell food and grains all by measure, by weight, in a known vessel, and by a known stone. Selling food and grains all by measure and by weight and in a known vessel and by a known stone. For example, food and grains that are present and of that kind, and not dirhams or dinars, can be sold in four ways mentioned in the text: (1) to sell them by measure; (2) to sell them by weight as well; (3) a vessel whose weight or measure is not known, but the seller and buyer agree that for that vessel they will give five pounds, so the sale is valid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a ruling statement listing the permissible methods for selling food and grains: by measure (kayl), by weight (wazn), by a known container (āniyah ma'lūmah), or by a known stone (hajar ma'lūm). The commentary explains that these are the four valid ways. The key is that the quantity must be known either through measurement, weight, or a specific container/stone whose capacity is known by custom or agreement. If the container's capacity is unknown, selling with it is not allowed unless the parties agree on a fixed price for that container, thus making the total price known.

Key Terms
مكالة (mukāyalah): Sale by measure (e.g., liters, bushels).
موزونة (mawzūnah): Sale by weight (e.g., kilograms).
آنية معلومة (āniyah ma'lūmah): A known vessel whose capacity is known by custom or agreement.
حجر معلوم (hajar ma'lūm): A known stone weight used as a standard measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) By a known stone (hajar ma'lūm)

Key Takeaway
Food and grains must be sold by one of four specified methods to ensure knowledge of quantity; otherwise the sale is invalid due to uncertainty.

Ruling on Unspecified Price in a Sale
Explains the ruling when no specific currency is mentioned in the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an unspecified price in a sale and apply the principle of custom (urf) to determine the currency, distinguishing between valid and invalid cases.

Core Idea
If no currency is specified, the dominant local currency is intended; if currencies are equal and different in value, the sale is invalid due to uncertainty.

When parties agree on a price but forget to mention which currency, confusion can arise. The Hanafi school addresses this by looking to the custom (urf) of the land. This lesson explores the ruling for such cases, including when the sale becomes invalid and how to rectify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Consider a sale where the price is mentioned without specifying the currency (mutlaq). The default ruling is that the price is interpreted as the dominant currency of the country (naqd al-balad).
This is based on the principle that custom (urf) is authoritative in commercial transactions.
2
Determine the effect of multiple currencies
If there are multiple currencies in circulation, check their prevalence and value. If one is clearly dominant, that currency is intended and the sale is valid.
Dominance is determined by what is commonly used in transactions.
3
Identify the invalid case
If the currencies are equally prevalent but differ in value, uncertainty (jahalah) arises because each party may prefer a different coin. This leads to potential dispute, so the sale is invalid (fasid).
The invalidity is due to the inability to determine the exact price, causing gharar.
4
Apply the remedy
If the parties specify a particular currency during the transaction council (majlis), the uncertainty is removed and the sale becomes valid.
This specification can occur at any point before the council ends.
5
Review the proof (dalil)
The passage cites a hadith of Aisha where the Prophet bought food with deferred payment without specifying the coin. This shows that deferred payment is allowed, but the price must be clear. Hanafis use custom to resolve ambiguity.
The hadith is ahad (single narrator) and zanni in transmission and meaning.
