The price in a sale, if left absolute, is based on the dominant currency of the country. If the currencies are different, one must be specified. [828] (9) It is permissible to sell all of food and grains by measurement and by estimation... This hadith indicates that deferred payment and cash both are allowed in sale. The proof is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet bought food from a Jew with deferred payment and pawned his armor. This shows that one can buy with deferred payment. The term must be fixed. The proof is the hadith in Bukhari number 1904. The date of payment must be fixed. If there is no dispute later, the sale becomes valid. The above hadith hints at that. Duration. In (8) if the price is left absolute, it follows the dominant currency. If currencies differ, the sale is invalid unless one is clarified. If they are equally common and one is not specified, if one coin is more prevalent, that is intended. If equal prevalence but different values, then due to ignorance the sale is invalid because the seller will demand the higher coin and the lower, and dispute arises. However, if at the time of the council the specific coin is indicated, then it becomes valid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the specification of price in a sale. The author states that when the price is mentioned in absolute terms without specifying a particular currency, it refers to the dominant currency of the city or country. If the currencies in circulation are different and one is not specified, the ruling depends on their prevalence and value. If one currency is clearly more common, that is the intended price and the sale is valid. If they are equally common but have different values, the sale becomes invalid (fasid) due to uncertainty (jahalah) because it can lead to dispute. However, if the parties indicate a specific coin during the transaction, the sale becomes valid. The author also cites a hadith from Aisha where the Prophet bought food from a Jew with deferred payment and pawned his armor, which proves the permissibility of deferred payment and the need to specify the term. The text emphasizes that the term (ajal) must be fixed to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
اطلق الثمن (utliqa al-thaman): When the price is mentioned in absolute terms without specifying the type of currency.
نقد البلد (naqd al-bald): The dominant currency of the country that is commonly used in transactions.
جہالت (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the price or item, which can render a sale invalid (fasid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The sale is automatically void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an absolute price in a sale is interpreted according to the dominant local currency, ensuring validity; only when currencies are equally prevalent and different in value does uncertainty invalidate the sale.

The Four Permissible Methods of Selling Food and Grains in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists four valid methods for selling food and grains with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four permissible methods of selling food and grains according to the Hanafi school and identify the condition that makes these methods valid.

Core Idea
Food and grain can be sold by measurement, estimation, or by an unknown container or stone, as long as it is present and of the same genus.

In Hanafi commercial law, the sale of food and grains enjoys flexibility to facilitate everyday transactions. This lesson presents four distinct methods recognized by the school, all of which are valid when the key condition of physical presence and known genus is met. Understanding these methods helps avoid invalid sales due to uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four methods
List from the text: (1) mukayalah (by measurement), (2) juzafan (by estimation), (3) using a specific container of unknown capacity, (4) using a specific stone of unknown weight.
2
Note the condition of presence
The item must be physically present at the time of sale. This eliminates gharar (uncertainty) about the object.
If the item is not present, the sale may be invalid.
3
Note the condition of known genus
The type (jins) must be known, and the item should not be dirhams or dinars (currency). Currency has its own rules.
Unknown genus leads to gharar.
4
Understand the rationale
Hanafis prioritize ease of transaction; estimation (juzaf) is allowed to avoid hardship, but only when the item is present so that both parties can see it.
Other schools may require exact measurement.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Shafi'is may require exact measurement; Hanafis allow estimation when the item is present.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز بيع الطعام والحبوب كلها مكايلة وجزافا وآناء بعينه لا يعرف مقداره او بوزن حجر بعينه لا يعرف مقداره [۸۲۸] (۹) کے کھانے اور غلوں سب کو بیچنا کیل کر کے اور انکل سے اور متعین برتن سے جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو یا متعین پتھر کے وزن سے جس کی مقدار و علائم نہ ہو۔ جو میچ کے موجود ہو اور غلہ اور کھانے کی جنس سے ہو، درہم اور دنا نیر نہ ہوں تو اس کو چار طریقوں سے بیچنا جائز ہے جن کا تذکرہ متن میں ہے میں ان کے بیچے (۲) الکل سے ویسے ہی بیچ دے یہ بھی جائز ہے (۳) ایک برتن ہے جس کا وزن یا کیل معلوم نہیں ہے کہ اس میں کیسے کیوں کے ہیں لیکن بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان یہ طے ہو گیا کہ ایک برتن کے بدلے پانچ پونڈ دوں گا تو بیع جائز ہو جائے حاشیه : ان میں سے ایک مدت تک کے لئے غلہ خریدا اور اس کے بدلے لوہے کی زرہ رہن رکھی۔
It is permissible to sell all of food and grains by measurement (kayl), by estimation (juzaf), by a specific container whose capacity is unknown, or by the weight of a specific stone whose weight is unknown. (9) Selling food and grains by measurement and by estimation, and by a specific container whose capacity is unknown, or by the weight of a specific stone whose weight is unknown. If the grain and food are present and of the same type, and not dirhams or dinars, then it is permissible to sell them in four ways. (2) It is also permissible to sell by estimation. (3) A container whose weight or measurement is unknown, but the seller and buyer agree that the container is worth five pounds, the sale becomes valid. Footnote: Among them, one buys grain for a fixed term and pawns an iron armor as security.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on the permissible methods of selling food and grains. The author lists four valid methods: (1) by measurement (kayl), (2) by estimation (juzaf) without precise measurement, (3) using a specific container whose exact capacity is unknown, and (4) using a specific stone whose weight is unknown. The key condition is that the item must be present (on the spot) and of the same genus (jins). The text also references a hadith that people in the Prophet's time used to buy food by estimation and were not allowed to sell it until they moved it to their dwellings, indicating the requirement of physical presence (qabd). The commentary explains that as long as the parties agree on the method, the sale is valid. The footnote mentions a case where grain is bought on credit and a metal armor is pawned.

Key Terms
مكايلة (mukayalah): Selling by measurement using a standard voluminous unit.
جزافا (juzafan): Selling by estimation without precise measurement or weight.
آناء بعينه (ina' bi'aynih): A specific container used as the measure, even if its exact capacity is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Food and grains can be sold by measurement, estimation, or by an unknown measure, provided the item is present and the genus is known.

The Sale of a Heap of Food per Qafiz: Abu Hanifa vs the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling a heap per unit without total quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of selling a heap of food per qafiz, identify the dalil for each, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When total quantity is unknown, Abu Hanifa limits validity to one unit; the Sahibayn validate the whole sale.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sale where the seller offers a heap of food at a price per unit (each qafiz for a dirham) without specifying the total quantity. This scenario raises a key issue in Islamic contract law: how much uncertainty (jahalah) is acceptable? We will compare the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and understand which position is relied upon in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the contracting terms
The seller says 'each qafiz for a dirham' for a heap of food. This creates a per-unit price but the total quantity (number of qafiz) is unknown.
2
Identify the legal problem
The problem is jahalah (ignorance) of the total price, which normally invalidates a sale in Islamic law because the price must be known.
The hadith of salaam requires a known measure and term.
3
Analyse the two Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: Only one qafiz is validly sold; the rest is void unless the seller later specifies the entire heap. Reason: total price is unknown (major jahalah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): The entire heap is validly sold. Reason: the unit price is known, the goods are present, and the total becomes known upon measuring; ignorance is minor.
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar allowing juzaf (estimation) sales when goods are present.
4
Determine the practical effect and tarjih
Practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Under Abu Hanifa, the buyer initially owns only one qafiz; for the rest, a new agreement is needed. Under the Sahibayn, the entire heap is sold from the start. Later Hanafi scholars prefer the Sahibayn's view (mufta bihi) because it facilitates transactions and reduces disputes.
The preference is based on ease and the principle that minor uncertainty is tolerated when goods are present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باع صبرة طعام كل قفيز بدرهم جاز البيع في قفيز واحد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله گی۔ مقدار کی جہالت سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑے گا۔ کیونکہ مبیع سامنے موجود ہے اس لئے اس کی مقدار نہ بھی معلوم ہو صرف انکل سے نیچے تب بھی جائز ہے (۴) اسی طرح ایک پتھر ہے جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے کہ کتنے کیلو وزن کا یہ پتھر ہے پھر بھی دونوں کے درمیان یہ ملے ہو جائے کہ ہر پتھر وزن کے بدلے پانچ پونڈ دوں گا تو بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ (1) جب انکل سے بیچنا جائز ہے تو اس طرح بھی بیچنا جائز ہوگا (۲) انکل سے بیچنے کی حدیث یہ ہے ان ابن عمر قال لقد رايت الناس في عهد رسول الله الله يبتاعون جزافا يعنى الطعام يضربون ان يبيعوا في مكانهم حتى يؤوه الى رحالهم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من رای اذا اشترى طعاما جزافا ان لا یبیعہ حتی 1 دیہالی رحله ص ۲۸۶ نمبر ۲۱۳۷ ر مسلم شریف ، باب بطلان بیع السريع قبل القبض ج ثانی ص ۵ نمبر ۱۵۲۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ انکل سے کھانا اور غلہ بیچنا جائز ہے اور اس وقت انکل سے نہیں بیچتے تھے جب تک کجاوے تک غلہ نہ آجائے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلہ سامنے موجود ہو تب ہی اٹکل سے بیچ سکتا ہے۔ اور سامنے موجود نہ ہو تو اس کی مقدار اور صفت کا متعین ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جیسے بخاری شریف اور مسلم شریف کی حدیث گزری من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم الى اجل معلوم ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۱۲۲۴۰ مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۶۰۴) نوٹ حدیث میں طعام کے لفظ سے یہ بھی پتہ چلا کہ درہم اور دنا نیر کو بغیر وزن کئے ہوئے نیچے تو اس میں تفصیل ہے۔ مكايلة : کیل کرکے۔ مجازفة : انکل سے۔ [۸۲۹] (۱۰) کسی نے کھانے کا ڈھیر بیچاہر فیز ایک درہم کے بدلے میں تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک قفیز کی بیع ہوگی اور باقی میں باطل ہوگی مگر یہ کہ تمام قفیر متعین کر دے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا دونوں سورتوں میں بیع جائز ہے۔
And whoever sells a heap of food, each qafiz for a dirham, the sale is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa. The ignorance of quantity does not affect because the goods are present. Even if the quantity is unknown, selling by estimation is permissible. (4) Similarly, a stone whose weight is unknown, if the parties agree to sell each stone for five pounds, the sale is valid. (1) When selling by estimation is permissible, then selling in this manner is also permissible. (2) The hadith of Ibn Umar: I saw people in the time of the Prophet buying food by estimation and they would not sell it in its place until they moved it to their dwellings. This shows that selling food by estimation is permissible, but only when the grain is present. If not present, the quantity and description must be specified. Also the hadith: 'Whoever gives a salaf in something, then it must be in a known measure and a known term.' Note: The word 'food' in the hadith indicates that dirhams and dinars are not included; there is detail. [829] (10) If someone sells a heap of food, each qafiz for a dirham, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the sale is valid only for one qafiz and the rest is void, unless he specifies all the qafiz. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the sale is valid in both cases.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The issue concerns selling a heap (sabrah) of food by stating 'each qafiz for a dirham' without specifying the total quantity or total price. According to Abu Hanifa, only the first qafiz is sold validly because the total price is unknown due to the unknown number of qafiz; the rest is invalid (batil) due to ignorance (jahalah) of the price. However, if the seller later specifies the entire heap, the sale becomes valid. The Sahibayn hold that the sale is valid for the entire heap because the unit price is known per qafiz, and the total becomes known after measuring; they consider the ignorance as minor (yaseer) since the goods are present. The text also provides hadith evidence for selling by estimation (juzaf) when the food is present, which supports the Sahibayn's view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is often the view of the Sahibayn due to ease of transactions.

Key Terms
صبرة طعام (sabrah ta'am): A heap or pile of food grains (like wheat) that is not measured.
قفيز (qafiz): A unit of volume/measure for grains, varying by region.
جاز البيع في قفيز واحد (jaza al-bay' fi qafiz wahid): The sale is valid only for one qafiz (according to Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a man sells a heap of wheat saying 'each qafiz for a dirham', how many qafiz are validly sold?
A) All of them
B) None of them
C) One qafiz
D) Half of them

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on per-unit sales of unmeasured heaps, but the relied-upon view validates the whole sale to facilitate transactions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Sale of Grain Pile per Unit: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on per-unit sale of unknown quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the sale of an unknown quantity of grain per unit, and identify the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
When the total is unknown, Abu Hanifa limits the sale to one unit; the Sahibayn allow the entire pile.

This passage addresses a classic dispute within the Hanafi school: the sale of a grain pile where each measure (qafiz) is priced individually without specifying the total number. At stake is whether the sale is valid for the entire pile or only for one unit. The ruling hinges on the role of presence (mushahada) versus precise knowledge of quantity. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract scenario
Understand exactly what is being sold: a pile of grain (sabrah) with each qafiz priced at one dirham, but the total number of qafiz is unknown. The price per unit is known, but the total consideration is not fixed.
This is distinct from selling the pile as a lump sum.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules that the sale is valid for only one qafiz (the definite minimum) and void for the remainder. His reasoning: uncertainty (gharar) in the total quantity invalidates the excess; only the certain minimum is enforceable.
He applies the principle that gharar in sales is prohibited.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the sale is valid for the entire pile. They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) based on the practice of buying by estimation (jizaf) during the Prophet's time, where presence of the commodity compensates for unknown quantity.
They argue that uncertainty can be resolved by subsequent measurement within the session.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa's view, if the pile contains 10 qafiz, the buyer only gets one qafiz unless they agree later. Under Sahibayn, the buyer gets the entire pile after measuring and paying accordingly.
This difference affects both parties' rights and obligations.
5
Evaluate the evidence
Both sides use the hadith of Ibn Umar on jizaf. Abu Hanifa sees it as allowing estimation only when the commodity is present, but not for an unknown total per unit. The Sahibayn see the hadith as endorsing estimation generally for present goods.
The exact wording of the hadith is key: it refrained from selling until the grain was brought to their camps.

1. Book of Sales. 'And selling by estimation (jizaf) or by a specific container whose quantity is unknown, or by a specific stone whose weight is unknown.' [829] (10) 'And whoever sells a pile of food, each qafiz for a dirham, then the sale is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and void for the rest unless he specifies the total number of qafiz. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is valid in both cases.' Commentary: Ignorance of quantity does not matter because the sold item is present; even if its quantity is unknown, selling by estimation is still valid. Similarly, if a stone of unknown weight is sold such that each weight unit is for five pounds, the sale is valid. The hadith proof for selling by estimation: Ibn Umar said, 'I saw people in the time of the Messenger of Allah buying food by estimation, and they would be struck not to sell it in their place until they brought it to their camps.' [Bukhari, Muslim] This shows that selling food and grain by estimation is permissible, but only if the grain is present; otherwise, its quantity and description must be specified. The hadith about salam: 'Whoever gives a salam for something, let it be for a known measure and a known term.' [Bukhari, Muslim] Note: The word 'food' in the hadith also indicates that selling dirhams and dinars without weighing requires detail. 'Mukayala': by measure. 'Mujazafa': by estimation. [829] (10) Someone sold a pile of food, each qafiz for a dirham. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid for one qafiz and void for the rest unless he specifies all the qafiz. The Sahibayn said it is valid in both cases. The pile is not measured, and its total price is unknown; it will be known after measuring. The seller says each qafiz is for one dirham, so Abu Hanifa considers only one qafiz sold. Since the total is unknown, the least is taken: one qafiz. If they later measure and agree on the total, then the entire pile is sold. Footnote (a): 'I saw people in the Prophet's time buying grain by estimation and refraining from selling it until it reached their camps.'

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a grain pile (sabrah) where each unit (qafiz) is priced separately. The issue is whether the entire pile can be sold when the total number of qafiz is unknown at the time of contract. Imam Abu Hanifa (RA) holds that the sale is valid only for one qafiz (the minimum) and void for the rest, unless the seller explicitly states the total quantity. His reasoning is that ignorance of the total quantity leads to uncertainty (gharar), which invalidates the sale beyond the definite unit. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the sale is valid for the entire pile because the uncertainty can be resolved later by measuring, and the parties have the ability to determine the total before the session ends. They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) based on the practice of buying by estimation (jizaf) in the Prophet's time, as evidenced by the hadith of Ibn Umar. The text also supports the permissibility of estimation when the commodity is present and visible, as opposed to absent items where precise specification is required. The ruling is based on the principle that presence of the item mitigates ignorance of quantity, but Abu Hanifa requires the total to be known at the time of contract to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
صبرة (sabrah): A pile of grain or food sold in bulk.
قفيز (qafiz): A unit of measurement for volume, used for grain.
جزاف (jizaf): Sale by estimation without precise measurement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The sale is valid for one qafiz only.
C) The sale is void entirely.
D) The sale is valid only if the buyer agrees to measure later.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the sale of a grain pile per unit without specifying the total is valid only for one unit according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn validate the entire pile by way of istihsan.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale of a Flock of Sheep Each for a Dirham
Ruling on sale of flock with individual pricing without total specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling a heterogeneous flock with per-unit pricing and explain why ignorance of total quantity invalidates the contract, citing the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Selling a flock of sheep at a per-dirham price is void because the total quantity is unknown, causing gharar.

In this passage, we examine a specific sale scenario: a flock of sheep sold at a fixed per-head price without specifying the total number. The Hanafi school rules this sale void (fasid) due to uncertainty in the total consideration. The proof draws from two hadiths – one forbidding the sale of a pile of dates of unknown measure, and another condemning cheating. We will also see how this case differs from the earlier grain case where the Sahibayn allowed subsequent measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a flock of sheep, each sheep priced at one dirham, without stating the total number of sheep. The Hanafi ruling (stated in the matn) is that the sale is fasid (void) for all sheep.
Fasid here means the contract does not effect ownership transfer until the defect (ignorance) is removed.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites two hadiths: (1) Jabir's hadith: the Prophet forbade selling a pile of dates of unknown measure for a specified measure of dates. (2) Abu Huraira's hadith: the Prophet condemned a food seller who hid moisture in the grain.
Both hadiths are ahad (single-narrator) and have zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith explicitly prohibits jahalah (ignorance) of quantity in a sale of dates, which is analogous to ignorance of the number of sheep. Analogy (qiyas) applies: the underlying illa (effective cause) is the uncertainty in the subject matter or price. The second hadith emphasizes that hidden defects (ghish) invalidate; here the varying quality of sheep (some fat, some thin) coupled with ignorance of total number leads to uncertainty about total price.
The analogy is strong because both cases involve essential uncertainty (gharar).
4
Note the ikhtilaf and its distinction
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) had a different view for grain (previous lesson): they allowed the sale if the parties could measure before the session ends. However, the text explicitly distinguishes sheep because sheep are heterogeneous (fat vs. thin). In grain, each unit is uniform; in sheep, the value varies, so ignorance of the total number leads to potential dispute. Therefore, the Sahibayn's ruling on grain does not extend to sheep.
This shows how the school considers the nature of the object (mutajans vs. mukhtalif).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that the sale is completely void (fasid) for all sheep. The ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The reasoning is consistent: any contract that leaves a material element (quantity) to future determination is invalid due to gharar.
Cross-madhhab: some schools might allow it if per-unit price is known, but Hanafis require total price certainty at contract.

جائیگی۔
اصول ان کا اصول یہ ہے کہ مجلس ختم ہونے سے پہلے ڈھیر کی مقدار اور اس کی مجموعی قیمت معلوم ہو جانے کا امکان ہوتب بھی جواز بیع کے لئے کافی ہے۔

۸۳۰ (۱۱) کسی نے بکری کا ریوڑ بیچا اس طرح کہ ہر بکری ایک درہم کی تو تمام ہی بکری میں بیع فاسد ہے۔
بکری میں تفاوت ہے کوئی موٹی ہے کوئی دبلی ہے اس لئے اوپر کے قاعدے کے اعتبار سے اگر ایک بکری کی بیع جائز قرار دیں تو جھگڑا ہو گا
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے کھجور کے اس ڈھیر کو بیچنے سے روکا جس کا کیل معلوم نہ ہو کیل کے ذریعہ متعین کھجور کے بدلے میں یعنی کھجور کے متعین کیل کے بدلے میں ایسے ڈھیر کو بیچنا جس کا کیل معلوم نہ ہو اس سے منع فرمایا (ب) حضور ایسے آدمی کے سامنے سے گزرے جو گیہوں بیچ رہے تھے ، آپ نے پوچھا کیسے بیچ رہے ہو تو انہوں نے حضور کو بتایا۔ آپ کو اے وحی آئی کہ اپنے ہاتھ کو گیہوں میں داخل کرے۔ تو آپ نے اس میں ہاتھ ڈالا تو گیہوں بھیگے ہوئے تھے۔ پس آپ نے فرمایا جو دھوکہ کرے وہ ہم میں سے نہیں ہے۔
(11) 'And whoever sells a flock of sheep, each sheep for a dirham, then the sale is void for all of them.' Commentary: The principle of Abu Hanifa is that before offer and acceptance, the entire pile and its total price must be known so that there is no ignorance at the time of offer. If there is ignorance of the quantity of the entire pile, selling is prohibited. Proof is in the hadith: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say, 'The Messenger of Allah forbade selling a pile of dates whose measure is unknown for a specified measure of dates.' [Muslim] This hadith shows that if the quantity of the pile is unknown, it cannot be sold due to ignorance. Another hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah passed by a man selling food, asked how he was selling, and he informed him; then revelation came to put his hand inside; he did so and found it wet; the Messenger said, 'He who cheats is not of us.' [Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi] This hadith also indicates that ignorance of quality is prohibited. Therefore, at the time of acceptance, if the quantity of the pile and its total price are unknown, the sale of the entire pile is not valid. It is necessary that the quantity and price be known at the time of acceptance. The Sahibayn say that it is in the hands of the seller and buyer to measure and know the total quantity and price; they can measure immediately and know the total price before the session ends, so there is no dispute. In their view, even if the total quantity is not stated before acceptance, the sale of the entire pile is valid. Their principle is that the possibility of knowing the quantity and total price before the session ends is sufficient for the permissibility of the sale. 'Sabrah': pile. 'Qafiz': a measure; its plural is 'qifzan'. [830] (11) Someone sold a flock of sheep, each sheep for a dirham, so the sale is void for all sheep. Because sheep differ; some are fat, some thin. According to the above principle, if one sheep were considered sold, there would be dispute. Footnote (a): The Prophet forbade selling a pile of dates whose measure is unknown for a specified measure of dates. (b): The Prophet passed a man selling wheat, put his hand inside and found it wet, and said, 'He who cheats is not of us.'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on selling a flock of sheep (or similar heterogeneous items) where each individual is priced equally without specifying the total. The matn states that such a sale is void (fasid) for all. The commentary explains the reasoning: ignorance (jahl) of the total quantity and total price at the time of contract invalidates the sale. The proof is from the hadith of Jabir which forbids selling a pile of dates of unknown measure for a specified measure of dates, as it leads to riba or gharar. Additionally, the hadith of Abu Huraira prohibits cheating (ghish) regarding hidden defects. Since sheep vary in value, pricing each identically without knowing the total leads to uncertainty about the consideration. The commentary also contrasts the earlier case of grain (where the Sahibayn allowed the sale based on subsequent measurement) but for sheep, the ruling remains void because the items are not uniform and the total is unknown. The hadith evidences are used to establish the necessity of knowledge (ilm) of the subject matter and price at the time of contract.

Key Terms
قطيع (qati'): A flock or herd of animals, here specifically sheep.
فاسد (fasid): Void, invalid in the sense that the contract does not effect transfer of ownership until rectified; it may be corrected by mutual agreement.
جہالت (jahalah): Legal ignorance or uncertainty regarding a material aspect of the contract, such as quantity or price.
صبرة (sabrah): A pile (of dates, grain, etc.), often used in the context of prohibited sales due to unknown measure.
غش (ghish): Cheating, fraud, or deception in a transaction, especially by concealing defects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the price per sheep is too low.
D) Because the seller did not specify the breed.

Key Takeaway
A sale with a per-unit price but unknown total quantity is fasid in Hanafi law due to gharar, even if the per-unit price is fixed.

Selling a Sabr Without Specifying Total Measure: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the sale of a sabr (pile) without specifying total measure, and apply the hadith proofs to identify the basis of each view.

Core Idea
A sale with jahala of total quantity is fasid under Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn accept it if measurement is possible before the session ends.

The sale of a pile (sabr) of grain without declaring its total measure raises a critical question: when must the quantity be known? This lesson presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. We will examine the hadith evidence and the underlying methodological difference that leads to contrasting rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
The base text (matn) states that the sale of a sabr is void (fasid) unless the total number of qafiz is named. This sets the default ruling.
The matn reflects Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the sale is valid whether the total is named or not. The commentary explains their reasoning: the jahala can be removed by measuring before the session ends.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: (1) Jabir's hadith forbidding sale of an unmeasured pile of dates for a known measure; (2) Abu Hurairah's hadith condemning fraud. Both support the requirement that the object's quantity be known.
The hadith of Jabir directly addresses ignorance of measure; the hadith of fraud implies full disclosure.
4
Understand the methodological difference
Abu Hanifa insists on actual knowledge at the moment of contract (offer and acceptance). The Sahibayn accept the mere possibility of measurement before the session concludes, deeming the sale valid if that condition is later fulfilled.
The dispute centers on whether the existence of jahala at the time of contract is fatal or curable by subsequent action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is void in the remainder unless he names the total of its qafiz. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is valid in both aspects. The principle of Abu Hanifa is that before offer and acceptance, the entire pile and its entire price must be known so that ignorance does not remain at the time of offer. If there is ignorance of the quantity of the entire pile, then selling it is prohibited. Its proof is in the hadith: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade selling a pile of dates without knowing its measure for a known measure of dates.' (Muslim) Also the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'The Messenger of Allah passed by a man selling food and asked him how he sells. He was inspired to put his hand inside, and found it wet. He said: He is not from us who cheats.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) So if at the time of acceptance the quantity and total price of the pile are not known, the sale of the whole pile is not valid. The Sahibayn say: The seller and buyer can quickly measure the pile and know its total price before the session ends; therefore, in their view, whether the total quantity is mentioned before acceptance or not, the sale of the entire pile is valid. Their principle is that as long as it is possible to know the quantity and total price before the session ends, it is sufficient for validity. (Glossary: sabra = pile, qafiz = a measure, plural qafzan.)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn regarding the sale of a pile (sabr) of grain: the sale is void unless the total number of measures (qafiz) is specified. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the sale is valid in both cases—whether the total is mentioned or not. The commentary then explains Abu Hanifa's principle: for a valid sale, both the quantity and price of the entire lot must be known at the time of offer and acceptance to eliminate jahala (ignorance). Two hadith are cited as proof: the hadith of Jabir forbidding the sale of an unmeasured pile of dates for a known measure, and the hadith of Abu Hurairah regarding the prohibition of fraud. These support the requirement that the object and price be known in detail. The Sahibayn's position relies on the possibility of measurement before the conclusion of the session (majlis). Thus, the disagreement hinges on whether the sale is contingent on actual knowledge at the moment of contract or merely on the possibility of removing ignorance before separation. The text also defines key terms: sabra (pile) and qafiz (a measure).

Key Terms
صبرة (sabra): A pile of grain or similar commodity sold in bulk without exact measurement.
قفیز (qafiz): A specific measure of volume, often used for grain.
جھالت (jahala): Ignorance of the quantity or quality of the object of sale, which renders the contract invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The price is not known.
D) The sale involves riba.

Key Takeaway
The key point is that in the Hanafi school, the sale of a sabr without naming total quantity is void according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn consider it valid if measurement is possible before the session ends; this divergence highlights the importance of timing in the requirement to eliminate jahala.

Ruling on Selling a Flock Per Head Without Specifying Total
Ruling on sale of flock per head

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for selling mixed-quality items per unit without specifying the total quantity, and explain why the sale is fasid.

Core Idea
Selling a flock of sheep at a fixed per-head price is invalid because disparity and unknown quantity cause dispute.

This lesson examines a nuanced sale scenario: a seller offers a flock of sheep, each sheep for one dirham, without stating the total number. The text rules the entire sale invalid and explains the reasoning. We will dissect the two defects and contrast with a valid case to understand the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction structure
The seller says 'each sheep for one dirham' (per head pricing) but does not specify how many sheep are in the flock.
No total price is set; price per unit is fixed but total depends on count.
2
Identify the two defects
First defect: ignorance of total quantity (jahala). Second defect: disparity (tafawut) among sheep—some fat, some thin—which would lead to dispute over which sheep is delivered.
Both defects independently invalidate the sale; combined they make it definitely fasid.
3
Contrast with uniform goods (wheat pile)
In an earlier case, selling one qafiz from a wheat pile was valid because wheat has no disparity; all grains are equal, so no dispute arises.
Uniformity eliminates the tafawut defect.
4
Derive the principle
When there is disparity among individual items and the sale of the entire lot was not made, the sale of even a single item is invalid due to likely conflict.
The principle prevents disputes that could arise from ambiguous delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۳۰] (۱۱) ومن باع قطيع غنم كل شاة بدرهم فالبيع فاسد في جميعها بکری میں تفاوت ہے کوئی موٹی ہے کوئی دبلی ہے اس لئے اوپر کے قاعدے کے اعتبار سے اگر ایک بکری کی بیع جائز قرار دیں تو جھگڑا ہو گا بائع دبلی دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری موٹی لینا چاہے گا۔ اس لئے ایک بکری بھی کی بیع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور پورے ریوڑ کی بیع اسلئے نہیں ہوگی کہ تمام ریوڑ کی تعداد معلوم نہیں اور نہ پورے ریوڑ کی بیع ہوئی ہے۔ اور گیہوں کے ڈھیر میں ایک قفیز کی بیع اس لئے جائز ہوگئی تھی کہ گیہوں میں تفاوت نہیں تمام گیہوں برابر ہیں اس لئے ایک قفیز جائز قرار دینے میں کوئی جھگڑا نہیں ہے۔ اصول افراد میں تفاوت ہو اور مجموعہ کی بیع نہ ہوئی ہو تو تفاوت کی وجہ سے ایک فرد کی بھی بیع نہیں ہوگی۔ قطيع : بکریوں کا مجموعہ، بکریوں کا ریوڑ ۔
(830) (11) And whoever sells a flock of sheep, each sheep for one dirham, then the sale is invalid in all of them. There is disparity among the sheep: some are fat, some thin. Therefore, according to the principle above, if one sheep were considered valid, there would be dispute: the seller would want to give a thin one and the buyer would want a fat one. Therefore, even the sale of one sheep is not valid. And the sale of the entire flock is not valid because the total number is not known, and the sale of the entire flock was not made. In the case of a pile of wheat, the sale of one qafiz was valid because there is no disparity among the wheat; all are equal, so there is no dispute in declaring one qafiz valid. The principle: when there is disparity among individuals and the sale of the total was not made, then due to disparity, the sale of even one individual is not valid. Qati: a collection of sheep, a flock.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling of this section: selling a flock of sheep with each sheep sold individually at a fixed price per head, without specifying the total number of sheep, renders the entire transaction invalid. The commentary explains that even a single sheep cannot be considered sold because there is disparity (tafawut) among the sheep: some are fat and some thin. If one sheep were sold, the seller would try to give a thin one and the buyer would demand a fat one, leading to conflict. The total sale is also invalid because the total quantity is unknown. The text distinguishes this from the earlier wheat pile case where one qafiz could be valid because all wheat is uniform—no disparity exists. The underlying principle: when there is disparity among individuals and no explicit sale of the entire lot, the sale of even a part is invalid due to potential dispute.

Key Terms
قطيع (qati'): A flock or group of livestock, especially sheep or goats.
تفاوت (tafawut): Disparity or difference in quality and value among items of the same type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Selling individual items at a fixed per-unit price is invalid if the total quantity is unknown and items differ in quality, due to risk of dispute.

Selling Cloth Per Cubit and Buying Food with Misdescribed Quantity
Ruling on selling cloth per cubit without specifying total length

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on selling cloth per cubit without specifying total length (invalid) and on buying a pile of food with a misstated quantity (buyer's option), and explain the underlying principles of jahala and khiyar.

Core Idea
Uncertainty (jahala) in total quantity or price invalidates a sale; when described quantity falls short, the buyer may rescind or accept proportionally.

This passage presents two related rulings from Hanafi fiqh on sales involving uncertainty. The first deals with selling cloth by the cubit without stating the total length: the sale is invalid because both quantity and total price are unknown, and disparity among cubits leads to potential dispute. The second concerns buying a pile of food described as a specific amount at a total price: if it turns out to be less, the buyer has the option (khiyar) to take the actual quantity at a proportional price or cancel the contract. These rulings illustrate the general principle that sales must be free from excessive uncertainty and that when a described attribute is missing, the affected party has a choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The source presents two cases: (a) selling cloth per cubit without naming total cubits, and (b) buying a pile of food assumed to be 100 qafiz but found less.
Both case involve uncertainty, but the ruling differs because of the nature of the subject matter.
2
Analyze the cloth sale
The cloth sale is invalid (fasid) because the total quantity and total price are unknown (jahala). Additionally, there is disparity in quality among cubits, which could cause dispute (niza') between seller and buyer.
If all cubits were uniform (e.g., modern factory cloth), a single cubit could be sold validly.
3
Analyze the food pile case
The food sale was originally valid because the total quantity (100 qafiz) and total price (100 dirhams) were known. When the actual quantity is less, the buyer has khiyar (option) to take the found quantity for its portion of the price or to rescind the contract.
If the quantity were more, the excess belongs to the seller (no option for the buyer to take extra).
4
Extract the general principle
When a sale involves a known total price for a described total quantity, any deviation gives the buyer an option. But when neither total quantity nor total price is fixed (as in the cloth case), the entire sale is void.
The principle differentiates between cases where the contract is valid but a description is unmet, and cases where the contract is fundamentally uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱ (۱۲) وكذلك من باع ثوبا مذارعة كل ذراع بدرهم ولم يسم جملة الذرعان [ ۸۳۲] (۱۳) ومن ابتاع صبرة طعام على انها مائة قفيز بمائة درهم فوجدها اقل من ذلك كان المشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذ الموجود بحضته من الثمن وإن شاء فسخ. بائع دبلی دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری موٹی لینا چاہے گا۔ اس لئے ایک بکری بھی کی بیع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور پورے ریوڑ کی پیج اسلئے نہیں ہوگی کہ تمام ریوڑ کی تعداد معلوم نہیں اور نہ پورے ریوڑ کی بیج ہوئی ہے۔ اور گیہوں کے ڈھیر میں ایک قفیز کی بیع اس لئے جائز ہوگئی تھی کہ گیہوں میں تفاوت نہیں تمام گیہوں برابر ہیں اس لئے ایک قفیز جائز قرار دینے میں کوئی جھگڑا نہیں ہے۔ اصول افراد میں تفاوت ہو اور مجموعہ کی بیچ نہ ہوئی ہو تو تفاوت کی وجہ سے ایک فرد کی بھی بیچ نہیں ہوگی۔ قطيع : بکریوں کا مجموعہ، بکریوں کا ریوڑ ۔ [۸۳۱] (۱۳) کسی نے کپڑا بچا گزروں کے حساب سے ، ہرگز ایک درہم کا اور تمام گز بیان نہیں کئے تو ایسے ہی کسی گز کی بیع جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ کپڑے کے تھان میں تفاوت تھا۔ ہر گز الگ الگ انداز کا تھا۔ اور پورے تھان میں کتنے گز ہیں یہ بیان نہیں کیا اور نہ پورے تھان کی . بیچ کی اور یوں کہا کہ ہر ایک گز ایک درہم کا تو پورے تھان کی بیچ اس لئے نہیں ہوگی کہ نہ اس کی پوری مقدار معلوم ہے اور نہ مجموعی قیمت معلوم ہے۔ اور ایک گز کی بیچ اس لئے نہیں ہوگی کہ ہرگز میں تفاوت ہے، بائع خراب اور گھٹیا گز دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری اعلی گز لینا چاہے گا اس لئے نزاع کی وجہ سے ایک گز کی بھی بیع نہیں ہوگی۔ اوپر گزر گیا۔ آج کل کی طرح تمام کپڑا ایک ہی انداز کا ہو تو ایک گز کی بیع ہو جائے گی، یا دوبارہ پورا تھان ناپ کر پورے تھان کی بیچ کر لے تب بھی از سر تو رضامندی کی وجہ سے پورے تھان کی بیچ ہو جائے گی اوپر کا فیصلہ تو خلاف کے وقت ہوگا۔ ہو مدارعة : ذراع سے مشتق ہے ہاتھ سے ناپ کر خود
(12) And similarly, whoever sells a cloth by cubit measurement (mudhara'a), each cubit for one dirham, and does not name the total of the cubits. (13) And whoever buys a pile of food assuming it is 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams, and then finds it less than that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take what is found for its portion of the price, or if he wishes, he may annul. The seller would want to give a thin one and the buyer would want to take a fat one. Therefore, even the sale of one sheep is not valid. And the sale of the entire flock is not valid because the total number is not known and the sale of the entire flock was not made. The principle: when there is disparity among individuals and the sale of the total was not made, then due to disparity, the sale of even one individual is not valid. Qati: a collection of sheep, a flock. (831) (13) Someone sold cloth by cubit, each cubit for one dirham, and did not mention all the cubits. Similarly, the sale of any cubit is not valid. There was disparity in the cloth; each cubit was of a different quality. He did not state how many cubits were in the entire cloth, nor did he sell the entire cloth. He only said: each cubit is for one dirham. So the sale of the entire cloth is not valid because neither its total quantity nor total price is known. And the sale of one cubit is not valid because there is disparity among cubits: the seller would want to give a bad and low-quality cubit, and the buyer would want to take a high-quality cubit, so due to conflict, even the sale of one cubit is not valid. This has passed above. In today's time, if all cloth is of the same quality, then the sale of one cubit is valid. Or if the entire cloth is measured again and the sale of the entire cloth is made with mutual consent, then it is valid. The earlier ruling applies when there is a dispute. Mudhara'a: derived from dhira' (cubit), measuring by hand.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings. The first (12) states: similarly, selling cloth by the cubit without stating the total number of cubits is invalid. The commentary explains that the cloth cubits are not uniform; there is disparity in quality. Without knowing the total length, both the total quantity and total price are unknown. Even a single cubit cannot be validly sold because the seller would deliver a poor cubit and the buyer would demand a good one, leading to dispute. The text notes that if all cubits are identical in quality (like modern cloth), then a single cubit can be sold. The second ruling (13) deals with buying a pile of grain described as 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams, but found to be less. The buyer has an option (khiyar): either take what exists for its proportional price or annul the contract. The commentary elaborates that since the total quantity and price were specified, the contract was valid, but when it turns out to be less, the buyer has a choice because the seller's description was not met. If the pile is found to be more, the excess belongs to the seller.

Key Terms
مذارعة (mudhara'a): Selling by cubit (dhira') measurement, i.e., per unit of length.
خراج (kharaj): Not directly used; rather the term for option (khiyar) is used.
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind a contract due to defect or misrepresentation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a buyer purchases a pile of food described as 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams but finds only 90 qafiz, what is the buyer's right according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must pay 100 dirhams and keep the 90 qafiz.
B) He can take 90 qafiz for 90 dirhams or cancel the contract.
C) He can demand 10 more qafiz from the seller.
D) The sale is automatically void.

Key Takeaway
Sales must be free from uncertainty (jahala) in essential terms; when a described quantity is lacking, the buyer may choose to accept a proportional reduction or rescind.

Buying a Pile of Food with Specified Quantity: The Buyer's Option When Deficient
Ruling on buyer's option when quantity is less than specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a purchased pile of grain is found to be less than the specified quantity and identify the buyer's option under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
When the quantity falls short, the buyer may accept the actual amount at the proportional price or rescind the sale.

In the third ruling of this chapter, the text addresses a common scenario: a buyer agrees to purchase a pile of grain described as 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams. The sale is valid because both quantity and price are known. But if measurement reveals a deficiency, the buyer is not forced to take the shortfall; he has a choice. This lesson explores the khiyar (option) granted to the buyer and the principle of proportional pricing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract's key terms
Note that the sale specifies both total quantity (100 qafiz) and total price (100 dirhams). This makes the contract valid and enforceable.
2
Determine the consequence when the quantity is less
If the pile contains less than 100 qafiz, the buyer has an option (khiyar): he may take the actual quantity and pay its proportionate share of the price, or he may cancel the sale entirely.
The proportionate price is calculated by the unit price implied by the contract, i.e., 1 qafiz per 1 dirham.
3
Understand the basis of the option
The seller's representation that the pile is 100 qafiz is not fulfilled. This gives the buyer the right to rescind because he did not get what was promised. The sale itself is not void; it is valid but with a defect in quantity.
This is different from khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) which applies when the goods have a hidden flaw. Here, the deficiency is a breach of description.
4
Note the ruling when the quantity exceeds
Although the matn is cut off, the commentary states that if the pile contains more than 100 qafiz, the excess belongs to the seller, as only the specified quantity was sold.
This follows the general principle of exact measurement: the buyer receives only what was contracted for.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳) ومن ابتاع صبرة طعام على انها مائة قفيز بمائة درهم فوجدها اقل من ذلك كان المشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذ الموجود بحضته من الثمن وإن شاء فسخ. ... ان غلے کا ڈھیر ہے اور بائع یوں کہہ رہا ہے کہ اس میں سو فیز گیہوں ہے سو درہم کے بدلے دوں گا۔ تو چونکہ پوری مقدار معلوم ہے اور مجموعی قیمت بھی سو درہم معلوم ہے اس لئے پورے ڈھیر کی بیچ ہوئی۔ لیکن جب نا پا تو سو فیز سے کم نکلا تو چونکہ بائع نے یہ بھی کہا تھا کہ سوفیز ہے اور سو درہم کے بدلے میں دوں گا تو ایک قفیز ایک درہم کا ہوا اس لئے اگر مثلا نوے قفیز نکلے تو نوے درہم لازم ہو نگے ۔ جتنا حصہ گیہوں ہے اتنا ہی حصہ ثمن لازم ہوگا۔ لیکن چونکہ سو فیز کی بات تھی اور مشتری کو اس سے کم ملاتو وعدہ کے مطابق نہیں ملا اس لئے اس کو اختیار ہو گا چاہے تو نوے در ہم سے نوے فیز لے اور چاہے تو بیع فسخ کردے۔ اور اگر گیہوں سو قفیز سے زیادہ نکلے تو چونکہ سو فیز ہی دینے کی بات تھی زیادہ کی نہیں اس
(13) And whoever buys a pile of food on condition that it is 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams, and then finds it less than that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take what exists for its portion of the price, or if he wishes, he may annul. ... That pile of grain: the seller says it contains 100 qafiz of wheat for 100 dirhams. Since the total quantity and total price are known, the entire pile has been sold. But when it was measured and found to be less than 100 qafiz, because the seller said it is 100 qafiz and will give it for 100 dirhams, one qafiz is for one dirham. So if, for example, 90 qafiz come out, then 90 dirhams are due. However, because the agreement was for 100 qafiz and the buyer did not get that, he has the option: he may take 90 qafiz for 90 dirhams, or he may annul the sale. And if the wheat comes out more than 100 qafiz, since the agreement was only for 100 qafiz, the excess belongs to the seller. This passage is cut off.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents the third ruling: if a buyer purchases a pile of grain described as 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams, the contract specifies both total quantity and price, so the sale is initially valid. Upon measurement, if the pile is found to contain less than 100 qafiz, the buyer has an option (khiyar). He can either accept the actual quantity and pay proportionately (e.g., 90 qafiz for 90 dirhams) or cancel the sale entirely. This is because the seller failed to deliver exactly what was promised, giving the buyer the right to rescind due to deficiency. If the pile is found to contain more than 100 qafiz, the extra belongs to the seller, as the contract was only for the specified amount. The commentary explains that the proportionality is based on the unit price implicit in the agreement.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind a contract due to deficiency or misrepresentation.
قفیز (qafiz): A measure of volume for grain.
بحضته (bi-haqqihi): For its portion; in proportion to the actual quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The buyer can take the 90 qafiz without paying anything.

Key Takeaway

Sale by Cubit Without Specifying Total: The Principle of Certainty
Ruling statement with analogical expansions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling cloth by the cubit without specifying the total, identify the underlying principle of uncertainty (gharar), and apply it to analogous cases like a herd of goats.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the total quantity is unknown and individual items differ — uncertainty in the subject matter voids the transaction.

In this lesson, we examine a specific sale scenario: a cloth sold by the cubit without specifying the total number of cubits. The ruling is not merely about cloth but establishes a broader legal principle about uncertainty (gharar) in sales. By understanding this case, you will learn how Hanafi law treats transactions where the subject matter is variable and the total is left unspecified, and you will be able to apply the same reasoning to similar cases like selling animals from a herd or grain from a heap.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What exactly is being sold? A cloth sold by the cubit (mudhara'a) without specifying the total number of cubits. The ruling: the sale is invalid (fasid). The author states 'sale does not occur' (بیع نہیں ہوگی).
The invalidity is due to uncertainty (gharar) in the subject matter.
2
Locate the Reason for Invalidity
Why is it invalid? Because the individual cubits differ in quality (thick vs. thin) and the total is unknown. This leads to dispute between buyer and seller. The key factor is variation (tafawut) among individuals combined with unspecified total.
The author mentions the seller wants to give thin cloth, buyer wants thick cloth — showing conflict.
3
Compare with the Uniform Case (Wheat)
The author contrasts with selling one qafiz from a heap of wheat. Since wheat is uniform (all equal), there is no dispute. Therefore, selling one qafiz from a heap is valid even if the total heap size is unspecified.
Uniformity eliminates uncertainty about quality, so the sale is valid.
4
Extend the Principle to a Herd of Goats
Applying the same reasoning: a herd of goats contains individuals that differ in quality. If the whole herd is not sold and the total number is unknown, even one goat cannot be validly sold because of the potential for dispute.
The author explicitly says 'not even one goat becomes sold'.
5
State the General Principle
The general principle derived: 'When there is difference in individuals and the whole was not sold, then due to difference the sale of even one individual is not valid.' This is the controlling rule for such transactions.
This principle is a key Hanafi rule in sales law concerning gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك من باع ثوبا مذارعة كل ذراع بدرهم ولم يسم جملة الذرعان بائع دبلی دینا چاہے گا اور مشتری موٹی لینا چاہے گا۔ اس لئے ایک بکری بھی کی بیع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور پورے ریوڑ کی پیج اسلئے نہیں ہوگی کہ تمام ریوڑ کی تعداد معلوم نہیں اور نہ پورے ریوڑ کی بیج ہوئی ہے۔ اور گیہوں کے ڈھیر میں ایک قفیز کی بیع اس لئے جائز ہوگئی تھی کہ گیہوں میں تفاوت نہیں تمام گیہوں برابر ہیں اس لئے ایک قفیز جائز قرار دینے میں کوئی جھگڑا نہیں ہے۔ اصول افراد میں تفاوت ہو اور مجموعہ کی بیچ نہ ہوئی ہو تو تفاوت کی وجہ سے ایک فرد کی بھی بیچ نہیں ہوگی۔ قطيع : بکریوں کا مجموعہ، بکریوں کا ریوڑ ۔
And likewise, whoever sells a cloth by the cubit, each cubit for a dirham, and does not specify the total number of cubits: the seller wants to give the thin one and the buyer wants to take the thick one. Therefore, not even one goat in a herd becomes sold. And the entire herd is not sold because the total number of the herd is unknown, and the entire herd was not sold. And in a heap of wheat, the sale of one qafiz is valid because there is no difference in wheat; all wheat is equal. There is no dispute in considering one qafiz valid. Principle: When there is difference in individuals and the whole was not sold, then due to difference the sale of even one individual is not valid. Qati': a collection of goats, a herd of goats.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the sale of cloth by the cubit (mudhara'a) without specifying the total number of cubits. The ruling states that such a sale is invalid because the individual cubits differ in quality (thick vs. thin), leading to conflict between buyer and seller. The author extends this principle to the sale of a herd of goats where individual animals differ; since the total is unknown and the sale was not of the whole herd, even one goat cannot be validly sold. Conversely, a heap of wheat is uniform, so selling one qafiz from it is valid. The underlying principle is that when individual items in a set differ and the whole set is not sold, the sale of a single item is invalid due to uncertainty and potential dispute.

Key Terms
مذارعة (mudhara'a): Selling by the cubit (arm's length) as a unit of measurement.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit, a unit of length approximately from elbow to fingertips.
قفيز (qafiz): A dry measure for grain, typically used for wheat.
قطيع (qati'): A herd or flock, specifically of goats or sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sale of one individual goat from an unspecified herd invalid in Hanafi law?
A) Because the herd is not owned by the seller
B) Because the individuals differ in quality and the total is unknown
C) Because goat meat is not permissible for sale
D) Because the price must be paid in gold

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, selling by unit (e.g., per cubit) without specifying the total quantity is invalid (fasid) when the units are not uniform, due to the risk of dispute.

Sale of a Heap of Grain with Specified Quantity and Price
Ruling on sale of a heap of grain with known quantity and price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale of a heap of grain with known quantity and price and explain the buyer's khiyar when the quantity differs.

Core Idea
In a sale of specified quantity, excess belongs to seller; deficiency gives buyer an option to adjust or cancel.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi sales law: buying a heap of grain with a stated total quantity and price. What happens when the actual quantity is more or less? The ruling hinges on the principle that each unit of a homogeneous commodity is a principal unit, not a description. The buyer's option preserves fairness without invalidating the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the sale of a sibra (heap) with known total quantity and price is valid (sahih). The passage deals with a sale of a heap of grain specified as 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams.
The validity requires that both quantity and price are known and agreed upon.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
If the buyer finds less than the specified quantity, he has an option (khiyar): take the existing quantity at a proportionate price or cancel the sale. If he finds more, the excess belongs to the seller without additional payment.
The option arises from the seller's promise, not from a defect in the contract.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Grain is homogeneous (each qafiz is identical), so each unit is a principal (asl) not a description (sifah). Therefore, the price is apportioned per unit. The excess units were not included in the sale and thus return to the seller.
This contrasts with goods where individual units differ (e.g., cloth), where the rule may differ.
4
Locate the proof
The passage cites an athar from Ikrimah: 'If you buy food and find it extra, the extra is for the seller, and the deficiency is on you.' This is a mursal narration but supports the Hanafi position.
The proof is zanni in both transmission and meaning, but sufficient for this ruling.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
The same rule applies to any homogeneous commodity sold by specified quantity and price. If the quantity is less, the buyer has an option; if more, the excess goes to the seller.
For heterogeneous goods, other rules may apply (e.g., option of defect).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ابتاع صبرة طعام على انها مائة قفيز بمائة درهم فوجدها اقل من ذلك كان المشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذ الموجود بحضته من الثمن وإن شاء فسخ. وان وجدها اكثر من ذلك فالزيادة للبائع کسی نے کھانے کا ڈھیر بیچا اس طرح کہ سو قفیز ہے سو درہم کے بدلے۔ پس اس کو اس سے کم پایا تو مشتری کو اختیار ہے چاہے تو موجود کو اس کے حصے کے مطابق ثمن سے لے لے اور چاہے تو بیع مسخ کر دے اور اگر سو فیز سے زیادہ پایا تو زیادہ بائع کے لئے ہے۔ ان غلے کا ڈھیر ہے اور بائع یوں کہہ رہا ہے کہ اس میں سو فیز گیہوں ہے سو درہم کے بدلے دوں گا۔ تو چونکہ پوری مقدار معلوم ہے اور مجموعی قیمت بھی سو درہم معلوم ہے اس لئے پورے ڈھیر کی بیچ ہوئی۔ لیکن جب نا پا تو سو فیز سے کم نکلا تو چونکہ بائع نے یہ بھی کہا تھا کہ سوفیز ہے اور سو درہم کے بدلے میں دوں گا تو ایک قفیز ایک درہم کا ہوا اس لئے اگر مثلا نوے قفیز نکلے تو نوے درہم لازم ہو نگے ۔ جتنا حصہ گیہوں ہے اتنا ہی حصہ ثمن لازم ہوگا۔ لیکن چونکہ سو فیز کی بات تھی اور مشتری کو اس سے کم ملاتو وعدہ کے مطابق نہیں ملا اس لئے اس کو اختیار ہو گا چاہے تو نوے در ہم سے نوے فیز لے اور چاہے تو بیع فسخ کردے۔ اور اگر گیہوں سو قفیز سے زیادہ نکلے تو چونکہ سو فیز ہی دینے کی بات تھی زیادہ کی نہیں اس لئے یہ زیادہ گیہوں بائع کے ہوں گے۔ اصول اس میں اصول یہ ہے کہ گیہوں ایک جیسے ہیں اس میں تفاوت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر قفیز اصل ہے صفت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر قفیز کے بدلے میں ایک درہم لازم ہوگا۔ اور زائد قفیز کی قیمت نہیں ملی اس لئے وہ بائع کے ہوں گے۔ اثر میں ہے سمع عكرمة يقول ان ابتعت . طعاما فوجدته زائدا قالزيادة لصاحب الطعام والنقصان علیک (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب اشتربیت طعاما فوجدته زائداج ثامن ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۱۴۶۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو کھانا زیادہ ہو وہ بائع کا ہوگا۔ سوال غلہ میں تیز اصل ہے صفت نہیں ہے۔ ابتاع : باغ سے مشتق ہے خریدا۔
And whoever buys a heap of grain on the condition that it is one hundred qafiz for one hundred dirhams, and he finds it less than that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes what is found with its share of the price, and if he wishes, he cancels the sale. And if he finds it more than that, the excess belongs to the seller. Someone sold a heap of grain in this manner: it is one hundred qafiz for one hundred dirhams. Then he found it less than that, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes the existing quantity with its corresponding share of the price, and if he wishes, he nullifies the sale. And if he finds it more than one hundred qafiz, then the extra is for the seller. This heap is grain, and the seller says it contains one hundred qafiz of wheat for one hundred dirhams. Since the total quantity is known and the total price is known (one hundred dirhams), the entire heap is sold. But when measured, it turned out less than one hundred qafiz. Since the seller said it is one hundred qafiz and he would give it for one hundred dirhams, each qafiz is for one dirham. So if, for example, ninety qafiz are found, ninety dirhams become obligatory. As much grain as there is, that much share of the price is obligatory. But since the agreement was for one hundred qafiz and the buyer got less, it is not according to the promise, so he has the option: if he wishes, he takes ninety qafiz for ninety dirhams, and if he wishes, he cancels the sale. And if the wheat comes out to more than one hundred qafiz, since the agreement was only to give one hundred qafiz, not more, this extra wheat belongs to the seller. Principle: In this, the principle is that wheat is uniform; there is no difference in it. Therefore, each qafiz is a principal (asl), not a description (sifah). Hence, for each qafiz, one dirham becomes obligatory. And the extra qafiz's price was not received, so they are for the seller. In a narration: It is narrated that Ikrimah said: 'If you buy food and find it extra, the extra is for the owner of the food, and the deficiency is on you.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on buying food and finding it extra, vol. 8, p. 133, no. 1461). This narration states that what is extra in food belongs to the seller. Question: In grain, the quality is principal, not description. 'Ibtā'a' is derived from 'bā'a', meaning 'he bought'.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a proof (athar). It addresses the sale of a heap of grain with a specified total quantity and price. The ruling: if the actual quantity is less, the buyer has the option (khiyar) to take the existing amount with a proportionate reduction in price or to cancel the sale. If the quantity is more, the excess belongs to the seller without additional payment. The commentary explains that each qafiz is considered a principal unit because grain is uniform; thus the price is apportioned per qafiz. An athar from Ikrimah is cited to support that extra quantity goes to the seller. The principle distinguishes this case from cloth where individual units differ; here, grain is homogeneous, so each qafiz is an independent unit of sale.

Key Terms
صبرة (sibra): A heap or pile of grain or similar commodity sold as a whole.
خيار (khiyar): Option; the right to either uphold or cancel the contract.
باع (bā'a): To sell; the root for 'mabī' (sold) and 'ibtā'a' (to buy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a heap of grain sold as 100 qafiz is found to be 90 qafiz?
A) The sale is void and both parties return their goods
B) The buyer must take 90 qafiz at the full price
C) The buyer has the option to take 90 qafiz at 90 dirhams or cancel the sale
D) The seller can force the buyer to take 90 qafiz at 100 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In a sale of a specific quantity of a homogeneous commodity, any excess belongs to the seller and any deficiency gives the buyer an option to take the lesser amount at a reduced price or cancel the sale.

Sale of Cloth or Land by Description: The Ruling When Size Varies
Ruling on sale of cloth or land by size description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a cloth or land sold with a described size is found to be less or more, and explain why the size is treated as a description, not a priced unit.

Core Idea
In Hanafi sales, a stipulated size is only a description, not a per-unit price, so no price adjustment occurs.

This lesson unpacks a key distinction in Hanafi sales law: when a cloth or land is sold with a specified length (e.g., ten cubits) for a lump sum, the size is merely a description to identify the item. If the actual size differs, the contract is not automatically adjusted; instead, the buyer gets an option when the size is less, and the seller cannot object when it is more. Understanding this ruling prevents confusion with cases where the unit is priced individually.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sale scenario
Recognize that the sale is for a specific item (cloth or land) with a described size and a total price, not a per-unit price.
Example: 'this cloth is ten cubits for ten dirhams' — the price covers the whole cloth.
2
Determine the actual size relative to the description
Compare the actual size found with the size mentioned. Two outcomes: less than described, or more than described.
If exactly as described, no issue; the sale proceeds normally.
3
Apply the ruling for less size
If the actual size is less, the buyer has an option (khiyar): he may take the item at the full price or cancel the sale.
This option arises because the buyer's satisfaction is diminished, not because of a defect.
4
Apply the ruling for more size
If the actual size is more, the buyer takes the entire item at the original price, and the seller has no right to demand extra or cancel.
The seller sold the whole item; additional size is a windfall for the buyer.
5
Understand the legal rationale (ta'lil)
The stipulated size is a description (sifah) for identification only; it is not a priced unit like in the grain case (where each measure has a price). Hence, no price adjustment per unit.
If the seller had said 'each cubit for one dirham', the cubit would be a principal (asl) and priced separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اشترى ثوبا على انه عشرة اذرع بعشرة دراهم او ارضا على انها مائة ذراع بمائة دراهم فوجدها اقل من ذلك فالمشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذها بجملة الثمن وان شاء تركها وان وجدها اكثر من الذراع الذى سماه فهى للمشترى ولا خيار للبائع کسی نے کپڑا خریدا اس طرح کہ وہ دس گز ہے دس درہم میں، یاز مین خریدی اس طرح کہ وہ سو گز ہے سو درہم میں پھر اس کو اس سے کم پایا تو مشتری کو اختیار ہے چاہے تو اس زمین اور کپڑے کو پوری ہی قیمت میں لے اور چاہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دے، اور اگر اتنے گز سے زیادہ پایا جتنا متعین کیا تھا تو وہ سب مشتری کا ہے۔ اور بائع کو روک لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ اوپر جیسا ہی ہے لیکن حکم میں فرق اس لئے ہے کہ کپڑے میں اور زمین میں گز سے نا پنا ایک صفت ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ صفت کے مقابلہ میں الگ سے کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے دس گزیا سو گز زمین صرف ترغیب کے لئے ہوئی ہر گز کے بدلے ایک درہم نہیں ہوا تو گویا کہ پورے تھان کپڑے کی قیمت دس درہم اور پورے زمین کے ٹکڑے کی قیمت سو درہم ہوئی چاہے تھان میں اور زمین میں گز زیادہ ہو یا کم ہو ۔ اس لئے لینا چاہے تو پورے دس درہم اور سو درہم دے کر پورا تھان اور پورا ٹکٹر از مین لے ۔ چاہے گز کم ہو چاہے زیادہ ہو۔ البتہ کم گز ہونے کی صورت میں مشتری کی رغبت کم ہے اس لئے اس کو چھوڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا اور زیادہ گر ہو جائے تو بائع کو روکنے کا اختیار اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ پورے تھان اور پورے ٹکڑے زمین کی بیع کر چکا ہے، چاہے جتنا ہو۔ نوں کپڑے اور زمین میں گز مفت ہے اور صفت کے مقابلہ میں الگ سے قیمت نہیں ہوتی جب تک کہ اس کو اصل نہ بنادیا جائے۔
And whoever buys a cloth on condition that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, or land on condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, and he finds it less than that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the total price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. And if he finds it more than the cubits which he specified, then it belongs to the buyer, and the seller has no option. Someone bought cloth in this manner: it is ten yards for ten dirhams, or land bought in this manner: it is one hundred yards for one hundred dirhams. Then he found it less, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes that land and cloth for the entire price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. And if he finds more than the yards which were specified, then all of it is for the buyer, and the seller has no right to withhold. This issue is similar to the above, but the difference in ruling is because, in cloth and land, measuring by yards is a description (sifah), and the rule is that no separate price is assigned to a description. Therefore, ten yards or one hundred yards of land were only for inducement; each yard was not for one dirham. So it is as if the total price of the entire cloth is ten dirhams and the total price of the entire piece of land is one hundred dirhams, whether the yards in the cloth or land be more or less. Hence, if he wishes to take, he gives the full ten dirhams and one hundred dirhams and takes the entire cloth and entire piece of land, whether the yards are less or more. However, in case of fewer yards, the buyer's inclination is less, so he has the option to leave. But if there are more yards, the seller has no option to withhold because he has sold the entire cloth and entire piece of land, whatever amount it is. So in cloth and land, the yard is free, and no separate price is assigned to the description unless it is made a principal (asl).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement distinguishing between two types of sales. When a cloth or land is sold with a description of its size (e.g., 'ten cubits for ten dirhams') without stipulating a price per unit, the size is merely a description, not a priced component. Therefore, if the actual size is less, the buyer has the option to take the item at the full price or leave it; if it is more, the buyer gets the extra without additional payment, and the seller cannot object. This differs from the previous grain case where each unit was priced individually. The commentary explains that in cloth and land, the stipulated size is only for encouragement, and the contract is for the whole item. The buyer's option when less is due to diminished satisfaction, not because of a price adjustment.

Key Terms
صفت (sifah): A description or attribute; in this context, the specified length is a description of the item, not a priced unit.
اصل (asl): Principal or foundation; when the unit is made a principal, it is priced separately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of a cloth described as ten cubits for ten dirhams, if the cloth is actually twelve cubits, what happens?
A) The buyer must pay twelve dirhams
B) The seller can take back the extra two cubits
C) The buyer gets the entire cloth for ten dirhams
D) The sale is void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a size description in a lump-sum sale is not a priced unit; the buyer gets the excess for free and has an option only if the size is less.
